<th scope="row">Designated</th>
<td>1946<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAHMDB_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAHMDB-4">[4]</a></sup></td>

<p><b>Pittsburgh</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>PITS</b>-burg</i></small></a>) is a city in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_(U.S._state)" title="Commonwealth (U.S. state)">Commonwealth</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">county seat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Allegheny County, Pennsylvania">Allegheny County</a>. As of 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> a total population of 305,704 lives within the city limits, making it the 63rd-<a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_cities_by_population" title="List of United States cities by population">largest city in the U.S.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Pop_Estimate_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Pop_Estimate-2">[2]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">metropolitan</a> population of 2,353,045 is the largest in both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ohio_Valley" title="Ohio Valley">Ohio Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">Appalachia</a>, the second-largest in Pennsylvania (behind <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Metropolitan_Statistical_Areas" title="List of Metropolitan Statistical Areas">26th-largest in the U.S.</a></p>
<p>Located at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio Rivers</a>, Pittsburgh is known as both "the Steel City" for its more than 300 <a href="/wiki/Steel" title="Steel">steel</a>-related businesses, and as the "City of Bridges" for its <a href="/wiki/Bridges_of_Pittsburgh" title="Bridges of Pittsburgh">446 bridges</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The city features <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of tallest buildings in Pittsburgh">30 skyscrapers</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_inclines_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of inclines in Pittsburgh">two inclines</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_Blockhouse" title="Fort Pitt Blockhouse">pre-revolutionary fortification</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Point_State_Park" title="Point State Park">Point State Park</a> at the confluence of the rivers. The city developed as a vital link of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">Atlantic coast</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-west#European_exploration_and_early_settlement" title="Mid-west">Midwest</a>, as the mineral-rich <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Mountains" title="Allegheny Mountains">Allegheny Mountains</a> made the area coveted by the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire#First_French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> empires, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunmore%27s_War" title="Dunmore's War">Virginians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whiskey_Rebellion" title="Whiskey Rebellion">Whiskey Rebels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Pittsburgh in the American Civil War">Civil War raiders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Aside from steel, Pittsburgh has led in manufacturing of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aluminum" title="Aluminum">aluminum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glass" title="Glass">glass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">foods</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports" title="Sports">sports</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transportation" title="Transportation">transportation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computing" title="Computing">computing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">autos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> For part of the 20th century, Pittsburgh was behind only <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> in corporate headquarters employment; it had the most U.S. stockholders <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> America's 1980s <a href="/wiki/Deindustrialization#United_States" title="Deindustrialization">deindustrialization</a> laid off area <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_worker" title="Blue-collar worker">blue-collar workers</a> and thousands of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">downtown</a> <a href="/wiki/White-collar_worker" title="White-collar worker">white-collar workers</a> when the longtime Pittsburgh-based world headquarters moved out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diaspora_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-10">[10]</a></sup> This heritage left the area with renowned <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">museums</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of hospitals in Pittsburgh">medical centers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Parks_Conservancy" title="Pittsburgh Parks Conservancy">parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/RIDC" title="RIDC">research centers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">libraries</a>, a diverse <a href="/wiki/Cultural_District,_Pittsburgh" title="Cultural District, Pittsburgh">cultural district</a> and the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bar_(establishment)" title="Bar (establishment)">bars</a> per capita in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ritenbaugh_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ritenbaugh-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Today, <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uber_(company)" title="Uber (company)">Uber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autodesk" title="Autodesk">Autodesk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> are among 1,600 technology firms generating $20.7 billion in annual Pittsburgh payrolls. The area has served as the long-time federal agency headquarters for <a href="/wiki/CERT_Coordination_Center" title="CERT Coordination Center">cyber defense</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_Engineering_Institute" title="Software Engineering Institute">software engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Robotics_Engineering_Center" title="National Robotics Engineering Center">robotics</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Energy_Technology_Laboratory" title="National Energy Technology Laboratory">energy research</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bettis_Atomic_Power_Laboratory" title="Bettis Atomic Power Laboratory">nuclear navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The area is home to <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of colleges and universities in Pittsburgh">68 colleges and universities</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> leaders <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edu_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-edu-14">[14]</a></sup> The nation's <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">fifth-largest bank</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies, and six of the top 300 U.S. law firms make their global headquarters in the Pittsburgh area, while <a href="/wiki/RAND_Corporation" title="RAND Corporation">RAND</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon" title="The Bank of New York Mellon">BNY Mellon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Chemicals" title="Nova Chemicals">Nova</a>, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Ground" title="FedEx Ground">FedEx</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayer_USA" title="Bayer USA">Bayer</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_for_Occupational_Safety_and_Health" title="National Institute for Occupational Safety and Health">NIOSH</a> have regional bases that helped Pittsburgh become the sixth-best area for U.S. job growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Pittsburgh was listed among the "eleven most livable cities in the world";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a>'</i>s <a href="/wiki/Global_Liveability_Ranking" title="Global Liveability Ranking">Global Liveability Ranking</a> placed Pittsburgh as the first- or second-most livable city in the United States in 2005, 2009, 2011, 2012 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The region is a hub for <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design</a>, sustainable energy, and energy extraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GrEn_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-GrEn-18">[18]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Pittsburgh" title="History of Pittsburgh">History of Pittsburgh</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etymology_of_Pittsburgh" title="Etymology of Pittsburgh">Etymology of Pittsburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Pittsburgh" title="Timeline of Pittsburgh">Timeline of Pittsburgh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG"><img alt=" A picture of the Fort Pitt blockhouse built by the British in 1764; it is the oldest extant structure in the City of Pittsburgh." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2576" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG/220px-Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG/330px-Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG/440px-Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bouquet_blockhouse.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:19em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background-color: #B0C4DE;">
<div class="" style="background-color: #B0C4DE; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">Historical claims</div>
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div><a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">French Empire</a> 1669–1758<br/>
<a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> 1681–1781<br/>
<a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> 1776–present</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh was named in 1758 by <a href="/wiki/John_Forbes_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Forbes (British Army officer)">General John Forbes</a>, in honor of British statesman <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt,_1st_Earl_of_Chatham" title="William Pitt, 1st Earl of Chatham">William Pitt, 1st Earl of Chatham</a>. The original pronunciation would have been <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>PITS</b>-brə</i></small></a> or <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>PITS</b>-bə-rə</i></small></a>, matching similarly named places in Great Britain such as <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> in Scotland and <a href="/wiki/Aldeburgh" title="Aldeburgh">Aldeburgh</a> in Suffolk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Pittsburgh was incorporated as a township in 1771 and as a <a href="/wiki/Borough_(Pennsylvania)" title="Borough (Pennsylvania)">borough</a> on April 22, 1794, with the following Act:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> "Be it enacted by the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_Senate" title="Pennsylvania State Senate">Pennsylvania State Senate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_House_of_Representatives" title="Pennsylvania House of Representatives">Pennsylvania House of Representatives</a> of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania...by the authority of the same, that the said town of Pittsburgh shall be...erected into a borough, which shall be called the borough of Pittsburgh for ever."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spell_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-spell-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current pronunciation, which is extremely unusual in English speaking countries, is almost certainly a result of a printing error in some copies of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/City_Charter" title="City Charter">City Charter</a> of March 18, 1816 (though not on the original document). The error was repeated commonly enough throughout the rest of the 19th century that the original pronunciation was lost and in 1890 the "h" was removed in order to make it easier to spell. After a public campaign the original spelling was officially restored by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Board_on_Geographic_Names" title="United States Board on Geographic Names">United States Board on Geographic Names</a> in 1911.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spell_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-spell-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The area of the Ohio headwaters was long inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a> and several other settled groups of <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The first known European to enter the region was the French explorer/trader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_de_La_Salle" title="Robert de La Salle">Robert de La Salle</a> from <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> during his 1669 expedition down the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> European pioneers, primarily Dutch, followed in the early 18th century. Michael Bezallion was the first to describe the forks of the Ohio in a 1717 manuscript, and later that year European <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">fur traders</a> established area posts and settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1749, French soldiers from <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> launched an expedition to the forks to unite Canada with <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">French Louisiana</a> via the rivers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronology_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-chronology-24">[24]</a></sup> During 1753–54, the British hastily built <a href="/wiki/Fort_Prince_George" title="Fort Prince George">Fort Prince George</a> before a larger French force drove them off. The French built <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne" title="Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a> based on LaSalle's 1669 claims. The <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a>, the North American front of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, began with the future Pittsburgh as its center. British General <a href="/wiki/Edward_Braddock" title="Edward Braddock">Edward Braddock</a> was dispatched with Major <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> as his aide to take Fort Duquesne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-25">[25]</a></sup> The British and colonial force were defeated at <a href="/wiki/Braddock%27s_Field" title="Braddock's Field">Braddock's Field</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Forbes_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Forbes (British Army officer)">General John Forbes</a> finally took the forks in 1758. Forbes began construction on <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_(Pennsylvania)" title="Fort Pitt (Pennsylvania)">Fort Pitt</a>, named after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_Pitt_the_Elder" title="William Pitt the Elder">William Pitt the Elder</a> while the settlement was named "Pittsborough".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lorant_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lorant-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_Rebellion" title="Pontiac's Rebellion">Pontiac's Rebellion</a>, native tribes conducted a <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_Pitt" title="Siege of Fort Pitt">siege of Fort Pitt</a> for two months until Colonel <a href="/wiki/Henry_Bouquet" title="Henry Bouquet">Henry Bouquet</a> relieved it after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bushy_Run" title="Battle of Bushy Run">Battle of Bushy Run</a>. Fort Pitt is notable as the site of an early use of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> for <a href="/wiki/Biological_warfare" title="Biological warfare">biological warfare</a>. Lord <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Amherst" title="Jeffrey Amherst">Jeffrey Amherst</a> ordered blankets contaminated from smallpox victims to be distributed in 1763 to the tribes surrounding the fort. The disease spread into other areas, infected other tribes, and killed hundreds of thousands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (November 2015)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>During this period, the powerful nations of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Iroquois Confederacy</a>, based in New York, had maintained control of much of the Ohio Valley as hunting grounds by right of conquest after defeating other tribes. By the terms of the 1768 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fort_Stanwix" title="Treaty of Fort Stanwix">Treaty of Fort Stanwix</a>, the <a href="/wiki/William_Penn" title="William Penn">Penns</a> were allowed to purchase the modern region from the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois</a>. A 1769 survey referenced the future city as the "Manor of Pittsburgh".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCC_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCC-29">[29]</a></sup> Both the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia" title="Colony of Virginia">Colony of Virginia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Province of Pennsylvania</a> claimed the region under their colonial charters until 1780, when they agreed under a federal initiative to extend the <a href="/wiki/Mason%E2%80%93Dixon_line" title="Mason–Dixon line">Mason–Dixon line</a> westward, placing Pittsburgh in Pennsylvania. On March 8, 1771 <a href="/wiki/Bedford_County,_Pennsylvania" title="Bedford County, Pennsylvania">Bedford County, Pennsylvania</a> was created to govern the frontier. On April 16, 1771, the city's first civilian local government was created as Pitt Township.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> William Teagarden was the first constable, and William Troop was the first clerk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a>, the village of Pittsburgh continued to grow. One of its earliest industries was boat building for settlers of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Country" title="Ohio Country">Ohio Country</a>. In 1784, Thomas Viceroy completed a town plan which was approved by the Penn family attorney. Pittsburgh became a possession of Pennsylvania in 1785. The following year, the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Post-Gazette" title="Pittsburgh Post-Gazette">Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</a></i> was started, and in 1787, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh Academy</a> was chartered. Unrest during the <a href="/wiki/Whiskey_Rebellion" title="Whiskey Rebellion">Whiskey Rebellion</a> of 1794 resulted in federal troops being sent to the area. By 1797, glass manufacture began, while the population grew to around 1,400. Settlers came via routes over the Appalachian Mountains or through the Great Lakes. <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_(Pennsylvania)" title="Fort Pitt (Pennsylvania)">Fort Pitt</a> (now Pittsburgh) at the source of the Ohio River became the main base for settlers moving into the <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territory" title="Northwest Territory">Northwest Territory</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg"><img alt=" A historic 1857 scene of the Monongahela River in downtown Pittsburgh featuring a steamboat" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="546" data-file-width="1000" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg/220px-Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg/330px-Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg/440px-Monongahela_River_Scene_Pittsburgh_PA_1857.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a> scene, 1857</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg"><img alt=" A wrought iron life-size facade of legendary steelworker Joe Magarac in downtown Pittsburgh" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="421" data-file-width="378" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d2/Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg/220px-Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d2/Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg/330px-Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d2/Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muralof300SixthStreetBuilding.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downtown facade memorializing Pittsburgh's <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">industrial heritage</a> with an image of legendary steelworker <a href="/wiki/Joe_Magarac" title="Joe Magarac">Joe Magarac</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> cut off the supply of British goods, stimulating American industry. By 1815, Pittsburgh was producing significant quantities of iron, brass, tin, and glass. On March 18, 1816, the 46-year-old local government became a city. In the 1830s, many <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh people</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merthyr" title="Merthyr">Merthyr</a> steelworks immigrated to the city following the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Rising" title="Merthyr Rising">Merthyr Rising</a>. By the 1840s, Pittsburgh was one of the largest cities west of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Mountains" title="Allegheny Mountains">Allegheny Mountains</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Fire_of_Pittsburgh" title="Great Fire of Pittsburgh">Great Fire of Pittsburgh</a> destroyed over a thousand buildings in 1845. The city rebuilt with the aid of Irish immigrants and by 1857, Pittsburgh's 1,000 factories were consuming 22 million coal bushels yearly. Coal mining and iron manufacturing attracted waves of European immigrants to the area.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> boosted the city's economy with increased iron and armament demand. <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> began steel production in 1875 at the <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Thomson_Steel_Works" title="Edgar Thomson Steel Works">Edgar Thomson Steel Works</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Braddock,_Pennsylvania" title="North Braddock, Pennsylvania">North Braddock, Pennsylvania</a>, which evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Steel_Company" title="Carnegie Steel Company">Carnegie Steel Company</a>. He adopted the <a href="/wiki/Bessemer_process" title="Bessemer process">Bessemer process</a> to increase production.</p>
<p>In 1901, Carnegie merged several companies into <a href="/wiki/U.S._Steel" title="U.S. Steel">U.S. Steel</a>. By 1910, Pittsburgh was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_cities_in_the_United_States_by_population_by_decade" title="Largest cities in the United States by population by decade">nation's 8th-largest city</a>, accounting for between a third and a half of national steel output. The city's population swelled to over a half million with European immigration via <a href="/wiki/Ellis_Island" title="Ellis Island">Ellis Island</a> in New York harbor. By 1940, non-Hispanic whites were 90.6% of the city's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Pittsburgh also became a main destination of the African-American <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a> from the rural South during the first half of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Limited initially by discrimination, some 95% percent of the men became unskilled steel workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, demand increased and area mills operated 24 hours a day to produce 95 million tons of steel for the war effort.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lorant_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lorant-26">[26]</a></sup> This resulted in the highest levels of air pollution in the city's almost century of industry. The city's reputation as the "arsenal of democracy"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> was being overshadowed by <a href="/wiki/James_Parton" title="James Parton">James Parton</a>'s 1868 observation of Pittsburgh being "hell with the lid off."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the war, the city launched a clean air and civic revitalization project known as the "Renaissance," cleaning up the air and the rivers. The "Renaissance II" project followed in 1977, focused on cultural and neighborhood development. The industrial base continued to expand through the 1970s, but beginning in the early 1980s both the area's steel and electronics industries imploded during national industrial restructuring. There were massive layoffs from mill and plant closures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diaspora_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-diaspora-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg"><img alt="President Obama visited Carnegie Mellon University's National Robotics Engineering Center in 2011 to demonstrations of cutting edge technology." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2392" data-file-width="3316" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg/220px-President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg/330px-President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg/440px-President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Obama_Visits_NREC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> visiting <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Robotics_Engineering_Center" title="National Robotics Engineering Center">National Robotics Engineering Center</a> in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the later 20th century, the area shifted its economic base to education, tourism, and services, largely based on healthcare/medicine, finance, and high technology such as robotics. Although Pittsburgh successfully shifted its economy and remained viable, the city's population has never rebounded to its industrial-era highs. While 680,000 people lived in the city proper in 1950, a combination of suburbanization and economic turbulence resulted in a decrease in city population, even as the metropolitan area population increased again.</p>
<p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_2000s_recession" title="Late 2000s recession">late 2000s recession</a>, Pittsburgh was economically strong, adding jobs when most cities were losing them. It was one of the few cities in the United States to see housing property values rise. Between 2006 and 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">Pittsburgh</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical area</a> (MSA) experienced over 10% appreciation in housing prices—the highest appreciation of the largest 25 MSAs in the United States, as 22 of the top 25 MSAs saw a depreciation of housing values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Pittsburgh's story of economic regeneration was the inspiration of President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> to host the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2009_G-20_Pittsburgh_summit" title="2009 G-20 Pittsburgh summit">2009 G-20 Pittsburgh summit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area#Regional_identity" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">Pittsburgh metropolitan area § Regional identity</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh has a total area of 58.3 square miles (151 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 55.6 square miles (144 km<sup>2</sup>) is land and 2.8 square miles (7.3 km<sup>2</sup>) (or 4.75%) is water. The <a href="/wiki/80th_meridian_west" title="80th meridian west">80th meridian west</a> passes directly through the city's downtown.</p>
<p>The city is on the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">Allegheny Plateau</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Allegheny_Plateau_(ecoregion)" title="Western Allegheny Plateau (ecoregion)">Western Allegheny Plateau</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown</a> area (also known as the Golden Triangle) sits where the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> flowing from the northeast and <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a> from the southeast form the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>. The convergence is at <a href="/wiki/Point_State_Park" title="Point State Park">Point State Park</a> and is referred to as "the Point." The city extends east to include the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shadyside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shadyside (Pittsburgh)">Shadyside</a> sections, which are home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">Library</a>, and many other educational, medical, and cultural institutions. The southern, western, and northern areas of the city are primarily residential.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4501" data-file-width="6741" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg/220px-Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg/330px-Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg/440px-Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Pittsburgh_from_Duquesne_Incline_in_the_morning.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown Pittsburgh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_Incline" title="Duquesne Incline">Duquesne Incline</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mt._Washington_(Pittsburgh)" title="Mt. Washington (Pittsburgh)">Mt. Washington</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pittsburgh_neighborhoods" title="List of Pittsburgh neighborhoods">Pittsburgh neighborhoods</a> are steeply sloped with two-lane roads. More than a quarter of neighborhood names make reference to "hills," "heights," or similar features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[a]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Steps_of_Pittsburgh" title="Steps of Pittsburgh">steps of Pittsburgh</a> comprise some 712 sets of outdoor public stairways with 44,645 treads and 24,090 vertical feet. They include hundreds of streets composed entirely of stairs, and many other steep streets with stairs for sidewalks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Many provide vistas of the Pittsburgh area while attracting hikers and fitness walkers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bike and walking trails have been built to border many of the city's rivers and hollows, but steep hills and variable weather can make <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">biking</a> a challenge. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Allegheny_Passage" title="Great Allegheny Passage">Great Allegheny Passage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Ohio_Canal" title="Chesapeake and Ohio Canal">Chesapeake and Ohio Canal</a> Towpath connect the city directly to downtown Washington, D.C. (some 335 miles (539 km) away) with a continuous bike/running trail.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Areas">Areas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Areas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pittsburgh_neighborhoods" title="List of Pittsburgh neighborhoods">List of Pittsburgh neighborhoods</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of tallest buildings in Pittsburgh">List of tallest buildings in Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_City_of_Pittsburgh_historic_designations" title="List of City of Pittsburgh historic designations">List of City of Pittsburgh historic designations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pittsburgh_History_and_Landmarks_Foundation_Historic_Landmarks" title="List of Pittsburgh History and Landmarks Foundation Historic Landmarks">List of Pittsburgh History and Landmarks Foundation Historic Landmarks</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="746" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg/300px-Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg/450px-Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg/600px-Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Pennsylvania_neighborhoods_fade.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pittsburgh's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Pittsburgh_neighborhoods" title="List of Pittsburgh neighborhoods">90 distinct neighborhoods</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city consists of the Downtown area, called the Golden Triangle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> and four main areas surrounding it. These surrounding areas are subdivided into distinct neighborhoods (in total, Pittsburgh contains 90 neighborhoods).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> Relative to downtown, these areas are known as the North Side, South Side/South Hills, East End, and West End.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Golden_Triangle">Golden Triangle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Golden Triangle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pitt_Skyline.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pitt_Skyline.jpg/220px-Pitt_Skyline.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pitt_Skyline.jpg/330px-Pitt_Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Pitt_Skyline.jpg/440px-Pitt_Skyline.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pitt_Skyline.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown Pittsburgh</a> from <a href="/wiki/Station_Square" title="Station Square">Station Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">Downtown Pittsburgh</a> has 30 skyscrapers, nine of which top 500 feet (150 m). <a href="/wiki/U.S._Steel_Tower" title="U.S. Steel Tower">U.S. Steel Tower</a> is the tallest at 841 ft (256 m).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cultural_District,_Pittsburgh" title="Cultural District, Pittsburgh">Cultural District</a> comprises a 14-block area of downtown along the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a>. It is packed with theaters and arts venues, and has a growing residential segment. Most significantly, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Cultural_Trust" title="Pittsburgh Cultural Trust">Pittsburgh Cultural Trust</a> is embarking on RiverParc, a four-block mixed-use "green" community, featuring 700 residential units and multiple towers between 20 and 30 stories. The <a href="/wiki/Firstside_Historic_District" title="Firstside Historic District">Firstside</a> portion of downtown borders the Monongahela River, the historic Mon Wharf and is home to the distinctive <a href="/wiki/PPG_Place" title="PPG Place">PPG Place</a> Gothic-style glass skyscraper complex. New condo towers have been constructed and historic office towers are converted to residential use, increasing 24-hour residents. Downtown is served by the <a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_Allegheny_County" title="Port Authority of Allegheny County">Port Authority</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_light_rail" title="Pittsburgh light rail">subway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bridges_of_Pittsburgh" title="Bridges of Pittsburgh">multiple bridges</a> leading north and south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> It is also home to <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_Pittsburgh" title="The Art Institute of Pittsburgh">The Art Institute of Pittsburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne University</a> which borders <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bluff_(Pittsburgh)" title="Bluff (Pittsburgh)">Uptown</a>.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Side">North Side</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: North Side">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/North_Side_(Pittsburgh)" title="North Side (Pittsburgh)">North Side (Pittsburgh)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buena_vista.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Buena_vista.JPG/220px-Buena_vista.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Buena_vista.JPG/330px-Buena_vista.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Buena_vista.JPG/440px-Buena_vista.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buena_vista.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The North Side</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The North Side is home to various neighborhoods in transition. What is known today as Pittsburgh's North Side was once known as <a href="/wiki/Allegheny,_Pennsylvania" title="Allegheny, Pennsylvania">Allegheny City</a>, and operated as a city independently of Pittsburgh. Allegheny City merged with Pittsburgh under great protest from its citizens. The North Side is primarily composed of residential neighborhoods and is noteworthy for well-constructed and architecturally interesting homes. Many buildings date from the 19th century and are constructed of brick or stone and adorned with decorative woodwork, ceramic tile, slate roofs and stained glass. The North Side is also home to many popular attractions such as <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a>, <a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Science_Center" title="Carnegie Science Center">Carnegie Science Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Aviary" title="National Aviary">National Aviary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol_Museum" title="Andy Warhol Museum">Andy Warhol Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mattress_Factory" title="Mattress Factory">Mattress Factory</a> installation art museum, <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Pittsburgh" title="Children's Museum of Pittsburgh">Children's Museum of Pittsburgh</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://randy.land/" rel="nofollow">Randyland</a>, Highmark SportsWorks, <a href="/wiki/Penn_Brewery" title="Penn Brewery">Penn Brewery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Observatory" title="Allegheny Observatory">Allegheny Observatory</a>. The North Side is also home to <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_General_Hospital" title="Allegheny General Hospital">Allegheny General Hospital</a>, which is listed among the 1999 <i>US News &amp; World Report</i> 2000 best hospitals nationwide.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Side">South Side</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: South Side">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/South_Side_(Pittsburgh)" title="South Side (Pittsburgh)">South Side (Pittsburgh)</a></div>
<p>The South Side was once the site of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">Pennsylvania Railroad</a> railyards and associated dense, inexpensive housing for mill and railroad workers. Since the late 20th century, the city undertook a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Main_Street_program&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Main Street program (page does not exist)">Main Street program</a> in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Historic_Preservation" title="National Trust for Historic Preservation">National Trust for Historic Preservation</a>, encouraging design and landscape improvements on East Carson Street, and supporting new retail. The area has become a local Pittsburgher destination. The South Side is one of the most popular neighborhoods in the city in which to own a home. The value of homes in the South Side has increased in value by about 10% annually for the past 10 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> East Carson Street has developed as one of the most vibrant areas of the city, packed with diverse shopping, ethnic eateries, vibrant nightlife, and live music venues.</p>
<p>In 1993 the <a href="/wiki/Urban_Redevelopment_Authority_of_Pittsburgh" title="Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh">Urban Redevelopment Authority of Pittsburgh</a> purchased the South Side Works steel mill property. It collaborated with the community and various developers to create a master plan for a mixed-use development, to include a riverfront park, office space, housing, health-care facilities, and indoor practice fields for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitt_Panthers" title="Pitt Panthers">Pitt Panthers</a>. Construction began in 1998. The <a href="/wiki/SouthSide_Works" title="SouthSide Works">SouthSide Works</a> has been open since 2005, featuring many stores, restaurants, offices, and the world headquarters for <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_Outfitters" title="American Eagle Outfitters">American Eagle Outfitters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="East_End">East End</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: East End">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg/220px-Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg/330px-Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg/440px-Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_in_Shadyside_Pittsburgh_PA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Shadyside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shadyside (Pittsburgh)">Shadyside neighborhood</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3934" data-file-width="4270" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg/220px-CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg/330px-CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg/440px-CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CMU_from_36th_floor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Library</a>, Museums of <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museum_of_Art" title="Carnegie Museum of Art">Art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Carnegie Museum of Natural History">Natural History</a> (foreground), <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> (background)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The East End is home to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlow_University" title="Carlow University">Carlow University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museums_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Museums of Pittsburgh">The Carnegie Institute's Museums of Art and Natural History</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frick_Art_%26_Historical_Center" title="Frick Art &amp; Historical Center">Frick Art &amp; Historical Center</a> (Clayton and the Frick art museum), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory" title="Phipps Conservatory">Phipps Conservatory</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soldiers_and_Sailors_Memorial_Hall" title="Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall">Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Zoo" title="Pittsburgh Zoo">Pittsburgh Zoo and PPG Aquarium</a>. The neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Shadyside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Shadyside (Pittsburgh)">Shadyside</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squirrel_Hill" title="Squirrel Hill">Squirrel Hill</a> are large, wealthy neighborhoods with some apartments and condos. They enjoy pedestrian-oriented shopping/business districts. <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a>, heavily populated by undergraduate and graduate students, is home to most of the universities, <a href="/wiki/Schenley_Park" title="Schenley Park">Schenley Park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Petersen_Events_Center" title="Petersen Events Center">Petersen Events Center</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_(Pittsburgh)" title="Bloomfield (Pittsburgh)">Bloomfield</a> is Pittsburgh's Little Italy and is known for its Italian restaurants and grocers. <a href="/wiki/Lawrenceville_(Pittsburgh)" title="Lawrenceville (Pittsburgh)">Lawrenceville</a> is a revitalizing rowhouse neighborhood popular with artists and designers; it is expected to benefit from the recent new construction of a new <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_of_Pittsburgh_of_UPMC" title="Children's Hospital of Pittsburgh of UPMC">Children's Hospital</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strip_District" title="Strip District">Strip District</a> to the west along the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> is an open-air marketplace by day and a clubbing destination by night.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="West_End">West End</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: West End">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/West_End_(Pittsburgh)#Region" title="West End (Pittsburgh)">West End (Pittsburgh) § Region</a></div>
<p>The West End includes <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington_(Pittsburgh)" title="Mount Washington (Pittsburgh)">Mt. Washington</a>, with its famous view of the Downtown skyline and numerous other residential neighborhoods such as <a href="/wiki/Sheraden_(Pittsburgh)" title="Sheraden (Pittsburgh)">Sheraden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elliott_(Pittsburgh)" title="Elliott (Pittsburgh)">Elliott</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicities">Ethnicities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ethnicities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Pittsburgh's patchwork of neighborhoods still retain an ethnic character reflecting the city's immigrant history. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>German</i>: <a href="/wiki/Troy_Hill_(Pittsburgh)" title="Troy Hill (Pittsburgh)">Troy Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Washington_(Pittsburgh)" title="Mount Washington (Pittsburgh)">Mt. Washington</a>, and <a href="/wiki/East_Allegheny_(Pittsburgh)" title="East Allegheny (Pittsburgh)">East Allegheny</a> (Deutschtown)</li>
<li><i>Italian</i>: <a href="/wiki/Brookline_(Pittsburgh)" title="Brookline (Pittsburgh)">Brookline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloomfield_(Pittsburgh)" title="Bloomfield (Pittsburgh)">Bloomfield</a> (Pittsburgh's Little Italy), <a href="/wiki/Morningside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Morningside (Pittsburgh)">Morningside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_(Pittsburgh)" title="Oakland (Pittsburgh)">Oakland</a></li>
<li><i>Hispanic/Latino</i>: <a href="/wiki/Beechview_(Pittsburgh)" title="Beechview (Pittsburgh)">Beechview</a>/<a href="/wiki/Brookline_(Pittsburgh)" title="Brookline (Pittsburgh)">Brookline</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, and the northern marginal regions of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, as well as northeastern <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Southside (Pittsburgh)">South Side</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lawrenceville_(Pittsburgh)" title="Lawrenceville (Pittsburgh)">Lawrenceville</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polish_Hill_(Pittsburgh)" title="Polish Hill (Pittsburgh)">Polish Hill</a></li>
<li><i>Lithuanian</i>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southside_(Pittsburgh)" title="Southside (Pittsburgh)">South Side</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uptown_(Pittsburgh)" title="Uptown (Pittsburgh)">Uptown (Pittsburgh)</a></li>
<li><i>African American/Multiracial African American</i>: <a href="/wiki/Hill_District_(Pittsburgh)" title="Hill District (Pittsburgh)">Hill District</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homewood_(Pittsburgh)" title="Homewood (Pittsburgh)">Homewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Larimer_(Pittsburgh)" title="Larimer (Pittsburgh)">Larimer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hazelwood_(Pittsburgh)" title="Hazelwood (Pittsburgh)">Hazelwood</a></li>
<li><i>Jewish</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashkenazi" title="Ashkenazi">Ashkenazi</a>): <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Squirrel_Hill" title="Squirrel Hill">Squirrel Hill</a></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_densities">Population densities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Population densities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several neighborhoods on the edges of the city are less urban, featuring tree-lined streets, yards and garages, with a more suburban character. Oakland, the South Side, the North Side, and the Golden Triangle are characterized by more density of housing, walking neighborhoods, and a more diverse, urban feel.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_identity">Regional identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Regional identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">Pittsburgh metropolitan area</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh falls within the borders of the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern United States</a> as defined by multiple US Government agencies, but the Pittsburgh <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Combined_Statistical_Area" title="Combined Statistical Area">Combined Statistical Area</a> extends into both the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">Southern United States</a> (<a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>), with the borders of the three regions meeting 30 miles (48 km) from the city. Pittsburgh is also in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_Megalopolis" title="Great Lakes Megalopolis">Great Lakes Megalopolis</a>, a collection of primarily Midwestern and nearby <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> cities, reflecting Pittsburgh's socio-economic connections to Ohio and points west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Briem_PG_2011_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Briem_PG_2011-51">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Petrucci_2013_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Petrucci_2013-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pittsburgh falls within the borders of <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">Appalachia</a> as defined by the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Regional_Commission" title="Appalachian Regional Commission">Appalachian Regional Commission</a>, and has long been characterized as the "northern urban industrial anchor of Appalachia."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> In its post-industrial state, Pittsburgh has been characterized as the "Paris of Appalachia",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> recognizing the city's cultural, educational, healthcare, and technological resources, as well as its status as Appalachia's largest city.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Pittsburgh lies in the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> zone (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Dfa</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> The city and river valleys lie in the USDA plant hardiness zone 6b while higher elevated areas lie in zone 6a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ars.usda.gov_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ars.usda.gov-59">[58]</a></sup> The area has four distinct seasons: winters are cold, cloudy, and moderately snowy, springs and falls generally mild with moderate levels of sunshine, and summers warm to hot and humid. As measured by percent possible sunshine, summer is by far the sunniest season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAAsun_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAAsun-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The warmest month of the year in Pittsburgh is July, with a 24-hour average of 72.6 °F (22.6 °C). Conditions are often humid, and combined with highs reaching 90 °F (32 °C) on an average 9.5 days a year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-61">[60]</a></sup> a considerable <a href="/wiki/Heat_index" title="Heat index">heat index</a> arises. The coldest month is January, when the 24-hour average is 28.4 °F (−2.0 °C), and lows of 0 °F (−18 °C) or below can be expected on an average 2.6 nights per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-61">[60]</a></sup> Officially, record temperatures range from −22 °F (−30 °C), on <a href="/wiki/1994_North_American_cold_wave" title="1994 North American cold wave">January 19, 1994</a> to 103 °F (39 °C), which occurred three times, most recently on July 16, 1988; the record cold daily maximum is −3 °F (−19 °C), which occurred three times, most recently the day of the all-time record low, while, conversely, the record warm daily minimum is 82 °F (28 °C) on July 1, 1901.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-61">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[b]</a></sup> Due to elevation and location on the windward side of the Appalachian Mountains, 100 °F (38 °C)+ readings are very rare, and were last seen on July 15, 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_61-4"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Average annual precipitation is 38.2 inches (970 mm) and total precipitation is greatest in May while least in October; annual precipitation has historically ranged from 22.65 in (575 mm) in 1930 to 57.41 in (1,458 mm) in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> On average, December and January have the greatest number of precipitation days. Snowfall averages 41.4 inches (105 cm) per season, but has historically ranged from 8.8 in (22 cm) in 1918–19 to 82.0 in (208 cm) in 1950–51.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> There is an average of 59 clear days and 103 partly cloudy days per year, while 203 days are cloudy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> In terms of annual percent-average possible sunshine received, Pittsburgh (45%) is similar to <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> (43%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_and_water_quality">Air and water quality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Air and water quality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:31em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: lightgray;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">"It's the best it's been in the lifetime for virtually every resident in this county...We've seen a steady decrease in pollution levels over the past decade and certainly over the past 20, 30, 40, 50 years or more."</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">Guillermo Cole</cite></div>
<p>In a 2013 ranking of 277 metropolitan areas in the United States, the <a href="/wiki/American_Lung_Association" title="American Lung Association">American Lung Association</a> (ALA) ranked only six U.S. metro areas as having higher amounts of short-term particle pollution, and only seven U.S. metro areas having higher amounts of year-round particle pollution than Pittsburgh. For ozone (smog) pollution, Pittsburgh was ranked 24th among U.S. metro areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup> The area has improved its air quality with every annual survey. The ALA's rankings have been disputed by the Allegheny County Health Department (ACHD), since data from only the worst of the region's 20 air quality monitors is considered by the ALA, without any context or averaging. The lone monitor used is located immediately downwind and adjacent to U.S. Steel's Clairton Coke Works, the nation's largest <a href="/wiki/Coke_(fuel)" title="Coke (fuel)">coke</a> mill, and several municipalities outside the city's jurisdiction of pollution controls, leading to possible confusion that Pittsburgh itself is the source or center of the emissions cited in the survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup> The region's readings also reflect pollution swept in from Ohio and West Virginia, though both are outside the jurisdictional powers of local leadership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the county was still below the "pass" threshold, the report showed substantial improvement over previous decades on every air quality measure. Fewer than 15 high ozone days were reported between 2007 and 2009, and just 10 between 2008 and 2010, compared to more than 40 between 1997 and 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[70]</a></sup> ACHD spokesman Guillermo Cole stated that "It's the best it's been in the lifetime for virtually every resident in this county...We've seen a steady decrease in pollution levels over the past decade and certainly over the past 20, 30, 40, 50 years, or more."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The local rivers continue to have pollution levels exceeding EPA limits; however, fish catches in the city in 2007 were found to be more than twice as free of pollutants than catches on the Canadian side of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a> and six times as free of pollutants than <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> catches of the New York border area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[72]</a></sup> There are other concerns about local storm sewers and waste treatment plants <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County_Sanitary_Authority#Pittsburgh.27s_sewer_overflow_problem" title="Allegheny County Sanitary Authority">frequently overflowing untreated sewage</a> into local waterways, due to flood conditions and antiquated infrastructure.</p>
<p>The city contains 31,000 trees on 900 miles of streets, by the last count conducted in 2005. A 2011 analysis of Pittsburgh's total tree cover, which involved sampling more than 200 small plots throughout the city, showed a value of between $10 and $13 million in annual benefits based on the "urban forest" contributions to aesthetics, energy use and air quality. Energy savings from shade, impact on city air and water quality, and the boost in property values were taken into account in the analysis. The city spends $850,000 annually on street tree planting and maintenance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[73]</a></sup></p>

<p>At the 2010 Census, there were 305,704 people residing in Pittsburgh, a decrease of 8.6% since 2000. 66.0% of the population was White, 25.8% Black or African American, 0.2% American Indian and Alaska Native, 4.4% Asian, 0.3% Other, and 2.3% mixed. 2.3% of Pittsburgh's population was of Hispanic or Latino origin of any race. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_Whites" title="Non-Hispanic Whites">Non-Hispanic Whites</a> were 64.8% of the population in 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-census1-81">[77]</a></sup> compared to 78.7% in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-82">[78]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_(5559872301).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3009" data-file-width="3009" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png/220px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png/330px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png/440px-Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_%285559872301%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Race_and_ethnicity_2010-_Pittsburgh_(5559872301).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of racial distribution in Pittsburgh, 2010 U.S. Census. Each dot is 25 people: <span style="color:#ff0000"><b>White</b></span>, <span style="color:#0000ff"><b>Black</b></span>, <span style="color:#00ff80"><b>Asian</b></span>, <span style="color:#ff8000"><b>Hispanic</b></span> or <b>Other</b> (yellow)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The five largest European ethnic groups in the city are German (19.7%), Irish (15.8%), Italian (11.8%), Polish (8.4%), and English (4.6%), while the metropolitan area is approximately 22% German-American, 15.4% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">Italian American</a> and 11.6% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish American</a>. Pittsburgh has one of the largest Italian-American communities in the nation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[80]</a></sup> the fifth-largest <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainian</a> community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[81]</a></sup> Pittsburgh has over 200,000 Croatian people making it the city with the most extensive <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">Croatian</a> community in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">ARDA</a> study, residents include 773,341 "Catholics"; 326,125 "Mainline Protestants"; 174,119 "Evangelical Protestants;" 20,976 "Black Protestants;" and 16,405 "Orthodox Christians," with 996,826 listed as "unclaimed" and 16,405 as "other" in the metro area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were 143,739 households, out of which 21.9% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 31.2% were married couples living together, 16.5% had a female householder with no husband present, and 48.4% were non-families. 39.4% of all households were made up of individuals and 13.7% had someone living alone who is 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.17 and the average family size was 2.95.</p>
<p>In the city, the population was spread out, with 19.9% under the age of 18, 14.8% from 18 to 24, 28.6% from 25 to 44, 20.3% from 45 to 64, and 16.4% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 36 years. For every 100 females there were 90.7 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 87.8 males.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Median_income" title="Median income">median income</a> for a household in the city was $28,588, and the median income for a family was $38,795. Males had a median income of $32,128 versus $25,500 for females. The per capita income for the city was $18,816. About 15.0% of families and 20.4% of the population were below the poverty line, including 27.5% of those under the age of 18 and 13.5% ages 65 or older.</p>
<p>In a 2002 study, Pittsburgh ranked 22nd of 69 urban places in the U.S. in the number of residents 25 years or older who had completed a bachelor's degree, at 31%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[84]</a></sup> Pittsburgh ranked 15th of the 69 places in the number of residents 25 years or older who completed a high school degree, at 84.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Metropolitan_Area" title="Pittsburgh Metropolitan Area">metro area</a> has shown greater residential <a href="/wiki/Racial_integration" title="Racial integration">racial integration</a> during the last 30 years. The 2010 census ranked 18 other U.S. metros as having greater black-white <a href="/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States" title="Racial segregation in the United States">segregation</a>, while 32 other U.S. metros rank higher for black-white isolation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US2010_report_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-US2010_report-90">[86]</a></sup> Within city limits both <a href="/wiki/Carlow_University" title="Carlow University">Carlow University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_College_Board_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_College_Board-91">[87]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-92">[88]</a></sup> have residential <a href="/wiki/Sex_segregation" title="Sex segregation">gender segregation</a> above 90%, as <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-93">[89]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-94">[90]</a></sup> both have female populations at 60% or greater. <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> has a 60% male population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-95">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
