<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:My_ountain_View.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pittsburgh skyline from Mount Washington</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh has adapted since the collapse of its century-long steel and electronics industries. The region has shifted to high technology, <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a>, health care, nuclear engineering, tourism, <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_technology" title="Biomedical technology">biomedical technology</a>, finance, education, and services. Total annual payroll of the region's technology industries, when taken in aggregate, exceeded $10.8 billion in 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[92]</a></sup> and in 2010 there were 1,600 technology companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bobkoff_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bobkoff-97">[93]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Economic_Research" title="National Bureau of Economic Research">National Bureau of Economic Research</a> 2014 report named Pittsburgh the second-best U.S. city for intergenerational economic mobility<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[94]</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American Dream</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[95]</a></sup> Reflecting the citywide shift from industry to technology, former factories have been renovated as modern office space. <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> has research and technology offices in a refurbished 1918–1998 <a href="/wiki/Nabisco" title="Nabisco">Nabisco</a> factory, a complex known as <a href="/wiki/Bakery_Square" title="Bakery Square">Bakery Square</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[96]</a></sup> Some of the factory's original equipment, such as a large dough mixer, were left standing in homage to the site's industrial roots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[97]</a></sup> Pittsburgh's transition from its <a href="/wiki/Industrial_heritage" title="Industrial heritage">industrial heritage</a> has earned it praise as "the poster child for managing industrial transition".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[98]</a></sup> Other major cities in the northeast and mid-west have increasingly borrowed from Pittsburgh's model in order to renew their industries and economic base.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[99]</a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:27em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: lightgray;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">Pittsburgh is the poster child for managing industrial transition.</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">Dr. Robert Mauro</cite></div>
<p>The largest employer in the city is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a>, with 48,000 employees. All hospitals, outpatient clinics, and doctor's office positions combine for 116,000 jobs, approximately 10% of the jobs in the region. An analyst recently observed of the city's medical sector: "That's both more jobs and a higher share of the region's total employment than the steel industry represented in the 1970s."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[100]</a></sup></p>

<p>Area retail is anchored by over 35 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_shopping_malls" title="Pittsburgh shopping malls">shopping malls</a> and a healthy downtown retail sector, as well as boutique shops along <a href="/wiki/Walnut_Street_(Pittsburgh)" title="Walnut Street (Pittsburgh)">Walnut Street</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Squirrel_Hill_(Pittsburgh)" title="Squirrel Hill (Pittsburgh)">Squirrel Hill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Station_Square" title="Station Square">Station Square</a>.</p>
<p>Education is another major industry in the region. The largest single employer in that industry is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>, with 10,700 employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Six <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> companies call the Pittsburgh area home. These include downtown's <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">PNC Financial Services</a>, <a href="/wiki/PPG_Industries" title="PPG Industries">PPG Industries</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Steel" title="U.S. Steel">U.S. Steel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kraft_Heinz" title="Kraft Heinz">The Kraft Heinz Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/WESCO_International" title="WESCO International">WESCO International</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Findlay_Township,_Pennsylvania" title="Findlay Township, Pennsylvania">Findlay Township, Pennsylvania</a> based <a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods" title="Dick's Sporting Goods">Dick's Sporting Goods</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[103]</a></sup> In 2006, <i>Expansion Magazine</i> ranked Pittsburgh among the top 10 metropolitan areas in the nation for climates favorable to business expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>The region is home to <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Technologies" title="Allegheny Technologies">Allegheny Technologies</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Eagle_Outfitters" title="American Eagle Outfitters">American Eagle Outfitters</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CONSOL_Energy" title="CONSOL Energy">CONSOL Energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kennametal" title="Kennametal">Kennametal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mylan" title="Mylan">Mylan</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayer_USA" title="Bayer USA">Bayer USA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a> operation headquarters. Other major employers include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BNY_Mellon" title="BNY Mellon">BNY Mellon</a>, <a href="/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline" title="GlaxoSmithKline">GlaxoSmithKline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermo_Fisher_Scientific" title="Thermo Fisher Scientific">Thermo Fisher Scientific</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lanxess" title="Lanxess">Lanxess</a>. The Northeast U.S. regional headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Chemicals" title="Nova Chemicals">Nova Chemicals</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deloitte_Touche_Tohmatsu" title="Deloitte Touche Tohmatsu">Deloitte Touche Tohmatsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Ground" title="FedEx Ground">FedEx Ground</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ariba" title="Ariba">Ariba</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/RAND_Corporation" title="RAND Corporation">RAND Corporation</a> call the area home. <a href="/wiki/84_Lumber" title="84 Lumber">84 Lumber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giant_Eagle" title="Giant Eagle">Giant Eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highmark" title="Highmark">Highmark</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rue_21" title="Rue 21">Rue 21</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Nutrition_Center" title="General Nutrition Center">General Nutrition Center</a> (GNC), CNX Gas (CXG), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genco_Supply_Chain_Solutions" title="Genco Supply Chain Solutions">Genco Supply Chain Solutions</a> are major non-public companies headquartered in the region. The global impact of Pittsburgh technology and business was recently demonstrated in several key components of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787 Dreamliner</a> being manufactured and supplied by area companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The nonprofit arts and cultural industry in Allegheny County generates $341 million in economic activity that supports over 10,000 full-time equivalent jobs with nearly $34 million in local and state taxes raised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>A leader in <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">environmental design</a>, the city is home to 60 total and 10 of the world's first <a href="/wiki/Green_building" title="Green building">green buildings</a> while billions have been invested in the area's <a href="/wiki/Marcellus_Formation#Economic_impact" title="Marcellus Formation">Marcellus</a> natural gas fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GrEn_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-GrEn-18">[18]</a></sup> A renaissance of Pittsburgh's 116-year-old film industry—that boasts the world's first <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_(movie_theater)" title="Nickelodeon (movie theater)">movie theater</a>—has grown from the long-running <a href="/wiki/Three_Rivers_Film_Festival" title="Three Rivers Film Festival">Three Rivers Film Festival</a> to an influx of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_films_and_television_shows_shot_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of films and television shows shot in Pittsburgh">major productions</a> including <a href="/wiki/Disney_Research" title="Disney Research">Disney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount</a> offices with the largest sound stage outside <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> and New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-Film-111">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pittsburgh has hosted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/INPEX_(invention_show)" title="INPEX (invention show)">INPEX</a>, the world's largest invention trade show annually since 1984,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[108]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tekko_(convention)" title="Tekko (convention)">Tekko</a> since 2003, <a href="/wiki/Anthrocon" title="Anthrocon">Anthrocon</a> since 2006, and <a href="/wiki/Developing_Unconventional_Gas" title="Developing Unconventional Gas">DUG East</a> energy trade show since 2009.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Pittsburgh" title="Culture of Pittsburgh">Culture of Pittsburgh</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Phipps6.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Phipps6.jpg/220px-Phipps6.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Phipps6.jpg/330px-Phipps6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Phipps6.jpg/440px-Phipps6.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Phipps6.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory" title="Phipps Conservatory">Phipps Conservatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3840" data-file-width="5760" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg/220px-Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg/330px-Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg/440px-Frick_Fine_Arts_Fountain_in_Oakland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="6000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png/220px-Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png/330px-Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png/440px-Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Skyline_Morning.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downtown Pittsburgh from the North Shore in the morning.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh has a rich history in arts and culture dating from 19th century industrialists commissioning and donating public works, such as <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Hall_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Heinz Hall for the Performing Arts">Heinz Hall for the Performing Arts</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Benedum_Center" title="Benedum Center">Benedum Center</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Pittsburgh Symphony Orchestra">Pittsburgh Symphony Orchestra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Opera" title="Pittsburgh Opera">Pittsburgh Opera</a>, respectively as well as such groups as the <a href="/wiki/River_City_Brass_Band" title="River City Brass Band">River City Brass Band</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Youth_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Pittsburgh Youth Symphony Orchestra">Pittsburgh Youth Symphony Orchestra</a>.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh has a long tradition of jazz, blues, and bluegrass music. The <a href="/wiki/National_Negro_Opera_Company" title="National Negro Opera Company">National Negro Opera Company</a> was founded in the city as the first all African-American opera company in the United States. This led to the prominence of African-American singers like <a href="/wiki/Leontyne_Price" title="Leontyne Price">Leontyne Price</a> in the world of opera. Pittsburgh has a number of small and mid-size arts organizations including the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Irish_and_Classical_Theatre" title="Pittsburgh Irish and Classical Theatre">Pittsburgh Irish and Classical Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quantum_Theatre" title="Quantum Theatre">Quantum Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_and_Baroque_Society_of_Pittsburgh" title="Renaissance and Baroque Society of Pittsburgh">Renaissance and Baroque Society of Pittsburgh</a>, and the early music ensemble <a href="/wiki/Chatham_Baroque" title="Chatham Baroque">Chatham Baroque</a>. Several choirs and singing groups are also present at the cities' universities; some of the most notable include the <a href="/wiki/Pitt_Men%27s_Glee_Club" title="Pitt Men's Glee Club">Pitt Men's Glee Club</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Chapel_Choir" title="Heinz Chapel Choir">Heinz Chapel Choir</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Dance_Council" title="Pittsburgh Dance Council">Pittsburgh Dance Council</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Ballet_Theater" title="Pittsburgh Ballet Theater">Pittsburgh Ballet Theater</a> host a variety of dance events. Polka, folk, square, and round dancing have a long history in the city and are celebrated by the world-famous <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University_Tamburitzans" title="Duquesne University Tamburitzans">Duquesne University Tamburitzans</a>, a multicultural academy dedicated to the preservation and presentation of folk songs and dance.</p>
<p>Hundreds of major films have been shot partially or wholly in Pittsburgh. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i> was largely filmed in Downtown, Oakland, and the North Shore. Pittsburgh has also teamed up with a Los Angeles-based production company, and has built the largest and most advanced movie studio in the eastern United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Film-111">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pittsburgh's major art museums include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol_Museum" title="Andy Warhol Museum">Andy Warhol Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museum_of_Art" title="Carnegie Museum of Art">Carnegie Museum of Art</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Frick_Art_%26_Historical_Center" title="Frick Art &amp; Historical Center">Frick Art &amp; Historical Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Center_for_the_Arts" title="Pittsburgh Center for the Arts">Pittsburgh Center for the Arts</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mattress_Factory" title="Mattress Factory">Mattress Factory</a>. The <a href="/wiki/ToonSeum" title="ToonSeum">ToonSeum</a>, one of three museums in the US dedicated to cartoon art, is located downtown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[109]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Carnegie Museum of Natural History">Carnegie Museum of Natural History</a> is the fourth ranked natural history museum in the US<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[110]</a></sup> and has extensive dinosaur, mineral, animal, and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt" title="Ancient Egypt">Egyptian</a> collections. The <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Science_Center" title="Carnegie Science Center">Carnegie Science Center</a> and associated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highmark_SportsWorks" title="Highmark SportsWorks">SportsWorks</a> has interactive technology and science exhibits. The <a href="/wiki/Heinz_History_Center" title="Heinz History Center">Senator John Heinz History Center and Western Pennsylvania Sports Museum</a> is a Smithsonian affiliated regional history museum located in the Strip District and its associated <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_Museum" title="Fort Pitt Museum">Fort Pitt Museum</a> is located in Point State Park. <a href="/wiki/Soldiers_and_Sailors_Memorial_Hall_and_Museum" title="Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall and Museum">Soldiers and Sailors Memorial Hall and Museum</a> in Oakland houses Western Pennsylvania military exhibits from the Civil War to present. The <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Pittsburgh" title="Children's Museum of Pittsburgh">Children's Museum of Pittsburgh</a> on the North Side features interactive exhibits for children. The eclectic <a href="/wiki/Bayernhof_Music_Museum" title="Bayernhof Music Museum">Bayernhof Music Museum</a> is six miles (9 km) from downtown while <a href="/wiki/The_Clemente_Museum" title="The Clemente Museum">The Clemente Museum</a> is located in the city's Lawrenceville section. The <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nationality_Rooms" title="Nationality Rooms">Nationality Rooms</a> showcase pre-19th century learning environments from around the world. There are regular guided and self-guided architectural tours in numerous neighborhoods. Downtown's cultural district hosts quarterly Gallery Crawls and the annual <a href="/wiki/Three_Rivers_Arts_Festival" title="Three Rivers Arts Festival">Three Rivers Arts Festival</a>. Pittsburgh is home to a number of art galleries and centers including the <a href="/wiki/Miller_Gallery_at_Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Miller Gallery at Carnegie Mellon University">Miller Gallery at Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frick_Fine_Arts_Building#University_Arts_Gallery" title="Frick Fine Arts Building">University Art Gallery</a> of the University of Pittsburgh, the <a href="/wiki/American_Jewish_Museum" title="American Jewish Museum">American Jewish Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wood_Street_Galleries" title="Wood Street Galleries">Wood Street Galleries</a>.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh is home to the popular amusement park <a href="/wiki/Kennywood" title="Kennywood">Kennywood</a>.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Zoo_and_PPG_Aquarium" title="Pittsburgh Zoo and PPG Aquarium">Pittsburgh Zoo and PPG Aquarium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phipps_Conservatory_and_Botanical_Gardens" title="Phipps Conservatory and Botanical Gardens">Phipps Conservatory and Botanical Gardens</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Aviary" title="National Aviary">National Aviary</a> have served the city for over a century.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh is home to one of the several state licensed casinos. The <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Casino_(Pittsburgh)" title="Rivers Casino (Pittsburgh)">Rivers Casino</a> is located on the <a href="/wiki/North_Shore_(Pittsburgh)" title="North Shore (Pittsburgh)">North Shore</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a>, just west of <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Science_Center" title="Carnegie Science Center">Carnegie Science Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a>.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh's <a href="/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a> is a recent artist to have a number one record. His anthem "<a href="/wiki/Black_and_Yellow" title="Black and Yellow">Black and Yellow</a>" (a tribute to Pittsburgh's official colors) reached number one on Billboard's "Hot 100"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[111]</a></sup> for the Week of February 19, 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[112]</a></sup> Not since Grammy-winning blues guitarist <a href="/wiki/George_Benson" title="George Benson">George Benson</a> has a Pittsburgh artist received such national acclaim. <a href="/wiki/Perry_Como" title="Perry Como">Perry Como</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a> are from Pittsburgh suburbs. Hip hop artist <a href="/wiki/Mac_Miller" title="Mac Miller">Mac Miller</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Slide_Park" title="Blue Slide Park">Blue Slide Park</a></i> debuted at the top of Billboard's album chart; its first #1 independent release since <i><a href="/wiki/Dogg_Food" title="Dogg Food">Dogg Food</a></i> in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_punk" title="Hardcore punk">Hardcore punk</a> acts, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aus_Rotten" title="Aus Rotten">Aus Rotten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anti-Flag" title="Anti-Flag">Anti-Flag</a>, originated in Pittsburgh.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh is home to the world's largest furry convention known as <a href="/wiki/Anthrocon" title="Anthrocon">Anthrocon</a>, which has been held annually at the <a href="/wiki/David_L._Lawrence_Convention_Center" title="David L. Lawrence Convention Center">David L. Lawrence Convention Center</a> since 2006. In 2013 Anthrocon drew over 5,000 visitors and had an economic impact of $6.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg/220px-Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg/330px-Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg/440px-Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_benedumcenter.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Benedum Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theatre_in_Pittsburgh" title="Theatre in Pittsburgh">Theatre in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<p>The city's first play was produced at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Market_Square,_Pittsburgh" title="Market Square, Pittsburgh">old courthouse</a> in 1803<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronology_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chronology-119">[115]</a></sup> and the first theater built in 1812.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-120">[116]</a></sup> Collegiate companies include the University of Pittsburgh's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Repertory_Theatre" title="University of Pittsburgh Repertory Theatre">Repertory Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kuntu_Repertory_Theatre" title="Kuntu Repertory Theatre">Kuntu Repertory Theatre</a>, Point Park University's resident companies at its <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Playhouse" title="Pittsburgh Playhouse">Pittsburgh Playhouse</a>, and Carnegie Mellon University's School of Drama productions and <a href="/wiki/Scotch%27n%27Soda" title="Scotch'n'Soda">Scotch'n'Soda</a> organization. The Duquesne University Red Masquers, founded in 1912, are the oldest, continuously producing theater company in Pennsylvania.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The city's longest-running theater show, <a href="/wiki/Friday_Nite_Improvs" title="Friday Nite Improvs">Friday Nite Improvs</a>, is an improv jam that has been performed in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Learning" title="Cathedral of Learning">Cathedral of Learning</a> and other locations for 20 years. The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_New_Works_Festival" title="Pittsburgh New Works Festival">Pittsburgh New Works Festival</a> utilizes local theatre companies to stage productions of original one-act plays by playwrights from all parts of the country. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Future_Ten" title="Future Ten">Future Ten</a> showcases new ten-minute plays. <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_Summer_Theatre" title="Saint Vincent Summer Theatre">Saint Vincent Summer Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Off_the_Wall_Productions" title="Off the Wall Productions">Off the Wall Productions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Playhouse" title="Mountain Playhouse">Mountain Playhouse</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Theatre_Factory&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Theatre Factory (page does not exist)">The Theatre Factory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stage_Right!" title="Stage Right!">Stage Right!</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Latrobe,_Pennsylvania" title="Latrobe, Pennsylvania">Latrobe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie,_Pennsylvania" title="Carnegie, Pennsylvania">Carnegie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennerstown,_Pennsylvania" title="Jennerstown, Pennsylvania">Jennerstown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trafford,_Pennsylvania" title="Trafford, Pennsylvania">Trafford</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greensburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Greensburg, Pennsylvania">Greensburg</a>, respectively, employ Pittsburgh actors and contribute to the culture of the region.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_fiction_set_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of fiction set in Pittsburgh">List of fiction set in Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_shot_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of films shot in Pittsburgh">List of films shot in Pittsburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_shows_shot_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of television shows shot in Pittsburgh">List of television shows shot in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Gertrude_Stein" title="Gertrude Stein">Gertrude Stein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Carson" title="Rachel Carson">Rachel Carson</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a> graduate from the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Springdale,_Pennsylvania" title="Springdale, Pennsylvania">Springdale, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[117]</a></sup> Modern writers include <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>-winning playwright <a href="/wiki/August_Wilson" title="August Wilson">August Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chabon" title="Michael Chabon">Michael Chabon</a> with his Pittsburgh-focused commentary on student and college life. Two-time Pulitzer Prize winner and recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_McCullough" title="David McCullough">David McCullough</a> was born and raised in Pittsburgh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Annie_Dillard" title="Annie Dillard">Annie Dillard</a>, a Pulitzer Prize–winning writer, was born and raised in Pittsburgh. Much of her memoir An American Childhood takes place in post-World War II Pittsburgh. <a href="/wiki/John_Edgar_Wideman" title="John Edgar Wideman">John Edgar Wideman</a> grew up in Pittsburgh and based "<a href="/wiki/Brothers_and_Keepers" title="Brothers and Keepers">Brothers and Keepers</a>," a National Book Critics awarded novel in his hometown. Poet <a href="/wiki/Terrance_Hayes" title="Terrance Hayes">Terrance Hayes</a>, winner of the 2010 National Book Award and a 2014 MacArthur Foundation Fellow, received his MFA from the University of Pittsburgh, where he is currently a faculty member. Poet <a href="/wiki/Michael_Simms_(publisher)" title="Michael Simms (publisher)">Michael Simms</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Autumn_House_Press" title="Autumn House Press">Autumn House Press</a>, currently resides in the Mount Washington neighborhood of Pittsburgh. Poet <a href="/wiki/Samuel_John_Hazo" title="Samuel John Hazo">Samuel John Hazo</a>, the first poet Laureate of the Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, also resides in the city. New writers include <a href="/wiki/Chris_Kuzneski" title="Chris Kuzneski">Chris Kuzneski</a> who attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> and mentions Pittsburgh in his works and Pittsburgher Brian Celio, author of <i>Catapult Soul</i> who captured the Pittsburgh 'Yinzer' dialect in his writing. Pittsburgh's unique literary style extends to playwrights,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[119]</a></sup> as well as local graffiti and hip hop artists.</p>
<p>There are also specific Pittsburgh genres that have been adopted in globally, from children's television to sci-fi/fantasy to <a href="/wiki/Yinzer" title="Yinzer">Yinzer</a> Pittsburghese.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh's position as the birthplace for community owned television and networked commercial television helped spawn the modern children's show genres exemplified by <i><a href="/wiki/Mister_Rogers%27_Neighborhood" title="Mister Rogers' Neighborhood">Mister Rogers' Neighborhood</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Where_in_the_World_Is_Carmen_Sandiego%3F_(TV_series)" title="Where in the World Is Carmen Sandiego? (TV series)">Where in the World is Carmen Sandiego?</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Happy%27s_Party" title="Happy's Party">Happy's Party</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cappelli_%26_Company" title="Cappelli &amp; Company">Cappelli &amp; Company</a></i>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Children%27s_Corner" title="The Children's Corner">The Children's Corner</a></i>, all nationally broadcast.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Dad" title="Pittsburgh Dad">Pittsburgh Dad</a></i> series has showcased the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburghese" title="Pittsburghese">Pittsburghese</a> genre to a global <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> audience since 2011.</p>
<p>The modern fantasy, macabre and science fiction <a href="/wiki/Genre" title="Genre">genre</a> was popularized by director <a href="/wiki/George_A._Romero" title="George A. Romero">George A. Romero</a>, television's <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cardille" title="Bill Cardille">Bill Cardille</a> and his <i><a href="/wiki/Chiller_Theatre_(Pittsburgh)" title="Chiller Theatre (Pittsburgh)">Chiller Theatre</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[120]</a></sup> director and writer <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Cundieff" title="Rusty Cundieff">Rusty Cundieff</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[121]</a></sup> and makeup effects guru <a href="/wiki/Tom_Savini" title="Tom Savini">Tom Savini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup> The genre continues today with the PARSEC writers organization,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[123]</a></sup> The It's Alive Show, the annual "Zombie Fest",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup> and several writer's workshops including Write or Die,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[125]</a></sup> Pittsburgh SouthWrites,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[126]</a></sup> and Pittsburgh Worldwrights<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[128]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Barton_Paul_Levenson" title="Barton Paul Levenson">Barton Paul Levenson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Chiacchia" title="Kenneth Chiacchia">Kenneth Chiacchia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Humphreys_Penrose" title="Elizabeth Humphreys Penrose">Elizabeth Humphreys Penrose</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_dialect">Local dialect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Local dialect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_English" title="Pittsburgh English">Pittsburgh English</a></div>
<p>The Pittsburgh English dialect, commonly called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_English" title="Pittsburgh English">Pittsburghese</a></i>, was influenced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">Scots-Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central European</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_European" title="Eastern European">Eastern European</a> immigrants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Locals who speak the dialect are sometimes referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Yinzer" title="Yinzer">Yinzers</a>" (from the local word "yinz" [var. <i>yunz</i>], a blended form of "you ones," similar to "y'all" and "you all" in the South). Common Pittsburghese terms are: slippy (slippery), redd up (clean up), jagger bush (thorn bush), and gum bands (rubber bands). The dialect is also notable for dropping the verb "to be." In Pittsburghese one would say "the car needs washed" instead of "needs to be washed," "needs washing," or "needs a wash." The dialect has some tonal similarities to other nearby regional dialects of Erie and Baltimore, but is noted for its somewhat <a href="/wiki/Staccato" title="Staccato">staccato</a> rhythms. The staccato qualities of the dialect are thought to originate either from Welsh or other European languages. The many local peculiarities have prompted <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> to describe Pittsburgh as, "the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galapagos_Islands" title="Galapagos Islands">Galapagos Islands</a> of American dialect."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> The lexicon itself contains notable loans from <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a> and other European languages; examples include <a href="/wiki/Headscarf" title="Headscarf">babushka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierogi" title="Pierogi">pierogi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Halu%C5%A1ky" title="Halušky">halušky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Livability">Livability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Livability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg/220px-Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg/330px-Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg/440px-Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_WEO_Night_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pittsburgh from the <a href="/wiki/West_End_Overlook" title="West End Overlook">West End Overlook</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh often places high in lists of the nation's most livable cities. After placing fourth and first in the first two editions of <i>Places Rated Almanac</i>, Pittsburgh finished third in 1989, fifth in 1993, 14th in 1997, and 12th in 2000, before reclaiming the number one spot in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlacesRated_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlacesRated-135">[131]</a></sup> The survey's primary author, David Savageau, has noted that Pittsburgh is the only city to finish in the top 20 of every edition.</p>
<p>In 2005, 2009, and 2011, Pittsburgh was named the most livable city in the United States and in those years, between the 26th- and 29th-most livable cities worldwide by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist2011_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-economist2011-136">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup> Pittsburgh ranked No. 28 in the book <i>Cities Ranked and Rated</i> (2004) by <a href="/wiki/Bert_Sperling" title="Bert Sperling">Bert Sperling</a> and Peter Sander.</p>
<p>In 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a></i> listed Pittsburgh as the most livable city in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-forbes.com_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-forbes.com-138">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-realestate.yahoo.com_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-realestate.yahoo.com-139">[135]</a></sup> A month later, <i>Forbes</i> named Pittsburgh the 7th best place to raise a family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup> Pittsburgh was ranked the 4th best city for working mothers by Forbes in 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup> and the city was ranked as one of the best for entrepreneurs by <i>Entrepreneur</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup> <i>Forbes</i> named Pittsburgh, in an 8-way tie, the world's 10th cleanest city for 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a></i> named Pittsburgh the top place to live in the United States in 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> and behind only <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a> for 2012 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was listed among the 10 best U.S. places to retire in 2012 by <i>CBS Money Watch</i> and <i>U.S. News</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> In February 2013 <i>Forbes</i> again placed Pittsburgh among its 10 most unexpectedly romantic world locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup> In April 2014, <a href="/wiki/Niche_(company)" title="Niche (company)">Niche</a> rated Pittsburgh the 15th best city for <a href="/wiki/Millennials" title="Millennials">millennials</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Livability rankings typically consider factors such as cost of living, crime, and cultural opportunities. Pittsburgh has a low cost of living compared to other northeastern U.S. cities. According to the Federal Housing Board the average price for a 3- to 4-bedroom, 2-bath family home in Pittsburgh for 2004 is $162,000, well below the national average of $264,540. Average 2010 rent for all bedrooms in Pittsburgh was $789. This compares to the nationwide average of $1,087.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[147]</a></sup> Pittsburgh also has five city parks and several parks managed by the Nature Conservancy, the largest of which, <a href="/wiki/Frick_Park" title="Frick Park">Frick Park</a>, provides a 664 acres (269 ha) of woodland park with extensive hiking and biking trails throughout steep valleys and wooded slopes. Birding enthusiasts love to visit Clayton Hill area of Frick Park, where well over 100 species of birds have been recorded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Enhancing Pittsburgh's livability is that the area faces little natural disaster risk such as an earthquake, hurricane, wildfire, or tornado. <i>Forbes</i> ranked Pittsburgh as having the 2nd lowest natural disaster risk in the nation for 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenburg_2009_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenburg_2009-153">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">Greater Pittsburgh</a> is not entirely free of natural disasters, however. Residents living in extremely low-lying areas near the rivers or one of the 1,400 creeks and streams experience occasional floods,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puko_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puko-154">[150]</a></sup> such as those caused when the remnants of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">Hurricane Ivan</a> hit rainfall records in 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[151]</a></sup> River flooding is relatively rare due to federal flood control efforts extensively managing locks, dams, and reservoirs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puko_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-Puko-154">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[153]</a></sup> Residents living near smaller tributary streams are less protected from occasional flooding, and the cost of a comprehensive flood control program for the region has been estimated at a prohibitive $50 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puko_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-Puko-154">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pittsburgh has the most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bar_(establishment)" title="Bar (establishment)">bars</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ritenbaugh_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ritenbaugh-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Pittsburgh" title="Sports in Pittsburgh">Sports in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh hosted the <a href="/wiki/History_of_American_football" title="History of American football">first professional football game</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1903_World_Series" title="1903 World Series">first World Series</a>. The city boasts several professional teams and in 2009 the city has won the <i><a href="/wiki/Sporting_News" title="Sporting News">Sporting News</a></i> title of "Best Sports City" in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hille_2010_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hille_2010-158">[154]</a></sup> and <i>Sperling's Best Places</i> "top 15 cities for baseball" in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup> College sports also have large followings with the University of Pittsburgh in football and sharing Division I basketball fans with Robert Morris and Duquesne.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh's dedication to sports has a long history with its major professional sports teams—the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Steelers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Penguins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pirates</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[156]</a></sup>—share the same team colors, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flag_of_Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Flag of Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">official city colors of black and gold</a>. This tradition of solidarity is unique to Pittsburgh. The black-and-gold color scheme has since become widely associated with the city and personified in its famous <a href="/wiki/Terrible_Towel" title="Terrible Towel">Terrible Towel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rails_to_Trails" title="Rails to Trails">Rails to Trails</a>", has converted miles of former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_tracks" title="Rail tracks">rail tracks</a> to recreational trails, including a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh-Washington_D.C._bike/walking_trail" title="Pittsburgh-Washington D.C. bike/walking trail">Pittsburgh-Washington D.C. bike/walking trail</a>. Several <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">mountain biking</a> trails are located within the city and suburbs, <a href="/wiki/Frick_Park" title="Frick Park">Frick Park</a> has biking trails and <a href="/wiki/Hartwood_Acres_Park" title="Hartwood Acres Park">Hartwood Acres Park</a> has many miles of <a href="/wiki/Single_track_(mountain_biking)" title="Single track (mountain biking)">single track</a> trails.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg/220px-Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg/330px-Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg/440px-Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pedro_goes_to_Pittsburgh.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:26em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: lightgray;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">[t]his is the perfect blend of location, history, design, comfort and baseball…The best stadium in baseball is in Pittsburgh.</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">ESPN</cite></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> baseball team, often referred to as the Bucs or the Buccos (derived from <a href="/wiki/Buccaneer" title="Buccaneer">buccaneer</a>), is the city's oldest professional sports franchise having been founded in 1881, and plays in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">Central Division</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>. The Pirates are nine-time Pennant winners and five-time <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> Champions, were in the first <a href="/wiki/1903_World_Series" title="1903 World Series">World Series (1903)</a> and claim two pre-World Series titles in 1901 and 1902. The Pirates play in <a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a>, annually ranked as one of the sports best venues; <a href="/wiki/ESPN.com" title="ESPN.com">ESPN.com</a> stated: "[t]his is the perfect blend of location, history, design, comfort and baseball…The best stadium in baseball is in Pittsburgh."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a> hosted the team's MLB record-tying fifth All-Star game in 2006.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh also has a rich <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negro_League" title="Negro League">Negro League</a> history, with the former <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Crawfords" title="Pittsburgh Crawfords">Pittsburgh Crawfords</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Homestead_Grays" title="Homestead Grays">Homestead Grays</a> credited with as many as 14 league titles and 11 Hall of Famers between them in the 1930s and 1940s, while the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Keystones_(baseball)" title="Pittsburgh Keystones (baseball)">Keystones</a> fielded teams in the 1920s. In addition, in 1971 the Pirates were the first Major League team to field an all-minority lineup. One sportswriter claimed, "No city is more synonymous with black baseball than Pittsburgh."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the late 20th century, the Pirates had three consecutive <a href="/wiki/National_League_Championship_Series" title="National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> appearances (1990–92) (going 6, 7 and 7 games each), followed by setting the MLB record for most consecutive losing seasons, with 20 from 1993 until 2012. This era was followed by three consecutive postseason appearances: the 2013 <a href="/wiki/National_League_Division_Series" title="National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> and the 2014-2015 Wild Card games. Their <a href="/wiki/1997_Pittsburgh_Pirates_season" title="1997 Pittsburgh Pirates season">September pennant race</a> in 1997 featured the franchises' last no-hitter and last award for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News_Executive_of_the_Year_Award" title="The Sporting News Executive of the Year Award">Sporting News' Executive of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/American_football_in_Western_Pennsylvania" title="American football in Western Pennsylvania">American football in Western Pennsylvania</a>.</div>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.
