<p>At the end of 2016, the Pittsburgh Bureau of Police reported 59 murders in the city, marking "one of the most violent years in recent history."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[173]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of colleges and universities in Pittsburgh">List of colleges and universities in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1098" data-file-width="822" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg/220px-HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg/330px-HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg/440px-HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HeinzSpireCathedral.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
University of Pittsburgh</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4101" data-file-width="7291" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg/220px-Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg/330px-Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg/440px-Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Carnegie_Mellon_Hamerschlag_Hall_and_Scott_Hall.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carnegie Mellon University</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh is home to many colleges, universities and research facilities, the most well-known of which are <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne University</a>. Also located in the city are <a href="/wiki/Carlow_University" title="Carlow University">Carlow University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Art_Institute_of_Pittsburgh" title="The Art Institute of Pittsburgh">The Art Institute of Pittsburgh</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Community_College_of_Allegheny_County" title="Community College of Allegheny County">Community College of Allegheny County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Theological_Seminary" title="Pittsburgh Theological Seminary">Pittsburgh Theological Seminary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Presbyterian_Theological_Seminary" title="Reformed Presbyterian Theological Seminary">Reformed Presbyterian Theological Seminary</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Institute_of_Mortuary_Science" title="Pittsburgh Institute of Mortuary Science">Pittsburgh Institute of Mortuary Science</a>.</p>
<p>The Greater Pittsburgh area is also home to four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_campus" title="Commonwealth campus">Commonwealth Campuses</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_State_University" title="Pennsylvania State University">Pennsylvania State University system</a> including <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Beaver" title="Penn State Beaver">Penn State Beaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Fayette,_The_Eberly_Campus" title="Penn State Fayette, The Eberly Campus">Penn State Fayette, The Eberly Campus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Greater_Allegheny" title="Penn State Greater Allegheny">Penn State Greater Allegheny</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_New_Kensington" title="Penn State New Kensington">Penn State New Kensington</a>.</p>
<p>The campuses of Carlow, Carnegie Mellon, and the University of Pittsburgh are located adjacent to each other in the Oakland neighborhood that is the city's traditional cultural center. Carnegie Mellon University (CMU) is a private research university founded by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> and is ranked 23rd overall on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_News_%26_World_Report" title="US News &amp; World Report">US News &amp; World Report</a></i> list of America's Best National Universities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usnews_college_rankings_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-usnews_college_rankings-181">[174]</a></sup> CMU is globally respected for its <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_School_of_Computer_Science" title="Carnegie Mellon School of Computer Science">School of Computer Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_College_of_Engineering" title="Carnegie Mellon College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tepper_School_of_Business" title="Tepper School of Business">School of Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_College" title="Heinz College">Heinz College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_College_of_Fine_Arts" title="Carnegie Mellon College of Fine Arts">College of Fine Arts</a>, writing, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_and_Decision_Sciences" title="Social and Decision Sciences">social and decision sciences</a>, information systems, statistics, and psychology programs. The University of Pittsburgh, established in 1787 and popularly referred to as "Pitt", is a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Commonwealth System of Higher Education">state-related</a> school with one of the nation's largest research programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edu_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-edu-14">[14]</a></sup> Pitt is ranked as the 20th national <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public university</a> by <i>US News &amp; World Report</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[175]</a></sup> and 62nd overall, and is known for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Graduate_School_of_Public_and_International_Affairs" title="University of Pittsburgh Graduate School of Public and International Affairs">University of Pittsburgh Graduate School of Public and International Affairs</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Information_Sciences" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Information Sciences">University of Pittsburgh School of Information Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swanson_School_of_Engineering" title="Swanson School of Engineering">Swanson School of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_College_of_Business_Administration" title="University of Pittsburgh College of Business Administration">University of Pittsburgh College of Business Administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Law">University of Pittsburgh School of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Social_Work" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Social Work">University of Pittsburgh School of Social Work</a>, and other biomedical and health-related sciences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usnews_college_rankings_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-usnews_college_rankings-181">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitt-fall-07_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitt-fall-07-185">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[179]</a></sup> Carlow University is a small private Roman Catholic university that while coeducational, has traditionally educated women. <a href="/wiki/Chatham_University" title="Chatham University">Chatham University</a>, a liberal arts women's college with coeducational graduate programs, is located in the Shadyside neighborhood, but also maintains a 388-acre (157 ha) Eden Hall Farm campus located in the <a href="/wiki/North_Hills,_Pennsylvania" title="North Hills, Pennsylvania">North Hills</a>. <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne University</a>, a private Catholic university located in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bluff_(Pittsburgh)" title="Bluff (Pittsburgh)">Bluff</a> neighborhood and is noted for its song and dance troupe, the <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University_Tamburitzans" title="Duquesne University Tamburitzans">Duquesne University Tamburitzans</a>, as well as programs in law, business, and pharmacy. <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a> was founded in 1961 and is well known for its Conservatory of Performing Arts and its <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Playhouse" title="Pittsburgh Playhouse">Pittsburgh Playhouse</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Public_Schools" title="Pittsburgh Public Schools">Pittsburgh Public Schools</a> teachers are paid well relative to their peers, ranking 17th in 2000 among the 100 largest cities by population for the highest minimum salary offered to teachers with a BA ($34,300).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Pittsburgh ranked fifth in the highest maximum salary offered to teachers with an MA ($66,380).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Local public schools include many charter and magnet schools, including <a href="/wiki/City_Charter_High_School" title="City Charter High School">City Charter High School</a> (computer and technology focused), Pittsburgh Montessori School (formerly Homewood Montessori), <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Gifted_Center" title="Pittsburgh Gifted Center">Pittsburgh Gifted Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_Academy_of_International_Studies_6-12" title="Barack Obama Academy of International Studies 6-12">Barack Obama Academy of International Studies 6-12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Creative_and_Performing_Arts_School" title="Pittsburgh Creative and Performing Arts School">Pittsburgh Creative and Performing Arts 6–12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Science_and_Technology_Academy" title="Pittsburgh Science and Technology Academy">Pittsburgh Science and Technology Academy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Pennsylvania_School_for_Blind_Children" title="Western Pennsylvania School for Blind Children">Western Pennsylvania School for Blind Children</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Pennsylvania_School_for_the_Deaf" title="Western Pennsylvania School for the Deaf">Western Pennsylvania School for the Deaf</a>.</p>
<p>Private schools in Pittsburgh include <a href="/wiki/Bishop_Canevin_High_School" title="Bishop Canevin High School">Bishop Canevin High School</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Catholic_High_School_(Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania)" title="Central Catholic High School (Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania)">Central Catholic High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Catholic_High_School" title="Oakland Catholic High School">Oakland Catholic High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winchester_Thurston_School" title="Winchester Thurston School">Winchester Thurston School</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Edmund%27s_Academy" title="St. Edmund's Academy">St. Edmund's Academy</a>, yeshiva schools and <a href="/wiki/The_Ellis_School" title="The Ellis School">The Ellis School</a>. <a href="/wiki/Shady_Side_Academy" title="Shady Side Academy">Shady Side Academy</a> maintains a PK–5 <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">primary school</a> campus in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Point_Breeze,_Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Point Breeze, Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">Point Breeze</a> neighborhood, in addition to its 6–12 middle and upper school campuses located in nearby suburban <a href="/wiki/Fox_Chapel,_Pennsylvania" title="Fox Chapel, Pennsylvania">Fox Chapel</a>. Other private institutions outside of Pittsburgh's limits include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Catholic_High_School" title="North Catholic High School">North Catholic High School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seton-La_Salle_Catholic_High_School" title="Seton-La Salle Catholic High School">Seton-La Salle Catholic High School</a>.</p>
<p>The city also has an extensive library system, both public and university. Most notable are the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Library_of_Pittsburgh" title="Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh">Carnegie Library of Pittsburgh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>'s University Library System, which rank 9th-largest (public) and 18th-largest (academic) in the nation, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Pittsburgh" title="Media in Pittsburgh">Media in Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_shot_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of films shot in Pittsburgh">List of films shot in Pittsburgh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_shows_shot_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of television shows shot in Pittsburgh">List of television shows shot in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Newspapers">Newspapers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Newspapers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KDKAGateway.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/KDKAGateway.jpg/220px-KDKAGateway.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/KDKAGateway.jpg/330px-KDKAGateway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/KDKAGateway.jpg/440px-KDKAGateway.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KDKAGateway.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
KDKA studios at Gateway Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are two major daily newspapers in Pittsburgh: the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Post-Gazette" title="Pittsburgh Post-Gazette">Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Tribune-Review" title="Pittsburgh Tribune-Review">Pittsburgh Tribune-Review</a></i>. Weekly papers in the region include the <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Business_Times" title="Pittsburgh Business Times">Pittsburgh Business Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_City_Paper" title="Pittsburgh City Paper">Pittsburgh City Paper</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Catholic" title="Pittsburgh Catholic">Pittsburgh Catholic</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jewish_Chronicle_of_Pittsburgh" title="The Jewish Chronicle of Pittsburgh">The Jewish Chronicle of Pittsburgh</a></i>, <i>The New People</i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/New_Pittsburgh_Courier" title="New Pittsburgh Courier">New Pittsburgh Courier</a></i>. Independent student-written university-based newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pitt_News" title="The Pitt News">The Pitt News</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tartan" title="The Tartan">The Tartan</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Duquesne_Duke" title="The Duquesne Duke">The Duquesne Duke</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_University" title="Duquesne University">Duquesne University</a>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Globe_student_newspaper" title="The Globe student newspaper">The Globe</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a>. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Law" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Law">University of Pittsburgh School of Law</a> is also home to <a href="/wiki/JURIST" title="JURIST">JURIST</a>, the world's only university-based legal news service.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Pittsburgh metro area is served by many local television and radio stations. The Pittsburgh <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Designated_market_area" title="Designated market area">designated market area</a> (DMA) is the 22nd-largest in the U.S. with 1,163,150 homes (1.045% of the total U.S.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nielsen_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-nielsen-188">[181]</a></sup> The major network television affiliates are <a href="/wiki/KDKA-TV" title="KDKA-TV">KDKA-TV</a> 2 (<a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>), <a href="/wiki/WTAE-TV" title="WTAE-TV">WTAE</a> 4 (<a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>), <a href="/wiki/WPXI" title="WPXI">WPXI</a> 11 (<a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>), <a href="/wiki/WPGH-TV" title="WPGH-TV">WPGH-TV</a> 53 (<a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>), <a href="/wiki/WPCW" title="WPCW">WPCW</a> 19 (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_CW_Television_Network" title="The CW Television Network">CW</a>), <a href="/wiki/WINP-TV" title="WINP-TV">WINP-TV</a> 16 (<a href="/wiki/Ion" title="Ion">Ion</a>), <a href="/wiki/WPNT" title="WPNT">WPNT</a> 22 (<a href="/wiki/MyNetworkTV" title="MyNetworkTV">MyNetworkTV</a>), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPCB" title="WPCB">WPCB</a> 40 (<a href="/wiki/Cornerstone_Television" title="Cornerstone Television">Cornerstone</a>). KDKA-TV, WPCW, WINP-TV, and WPCB are network owned-and-operated stations. <a href="/wiki/WEPA-CD" title="WEPA-CD">WEPA-CD</a> 16 is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_station" title="Independent station">independent station</a> owned and operated by the Bruno-Goodworth Network.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/WQED_(TV)" title="WQED (TV)">WQED</a> 13 is the local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">PBS</a> station in Pittsburgh. It was established on April 1, 1954, and was the first community-sponsored television station and the fifth public station in the United States. The station has produced much original content for PBS, including <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mr._Rogers%27_Neighborhood" title="Mr. Rogers' Neighborhood">Mr. Rogers' Neighborhood</a></i>, several <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Society" title="National Geographic Society">National Geographic</a> specials, and <i><a href="/wiki/Where_in_the_World_Is_Carmen_Sandiego%3F_(game_show)" title="Where in the World Is Carmen Sandiego? (game show)">Where in the World is Carmen Sandiego?</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WQED_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-WQED-189">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio stations</a> serving the Pittsburgh market. The first was <a href="/wiki/KDKA_(AM)" title="KDKA (AM)">KDKA</a> 1020 AM, also the world's first commercially licensed radio station, airing on November 2, 1920.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KDKA_AM_1020_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-KDKA_AM_1020-190">[183]</a></sup> Other popular stations include <a href="/wiki/KQV" title="KQV">KQV</a> 1410 AM (news), <a href="/wiki/WBGG_(AM)" title="WBGG (AM)">WBGG</a> 970 AM (sports), <a href="/wiki/KDKA-FM" title="KDKA-FM">KDKA-FM</a> 93.7 FM (sports), <a href="/wiki/WKST-FM" title="WKST-FM">WKST-FM</a> 96.1 FM (pop and hip-hop), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WAMO-AM" title="WAMO-AM">WAMO-AM</a> 660 AM (hip-hop and R&amp;B) <a href="/wiki/WBZZ" title="WBZZ">WBZZ</a> 100.7 FM (adult contemporary), <a href="/wiki/WDVE" title="WDVE">WDVE</a> 102.5 FM (album rock), <a href="/wiki/WPGB" title="WPGB">WPGB</a> 104.7 FM (Country), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WXDX" title="WXDX">WXDX</a> 105.9 FM (modern rock). There are also three <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">public radio stations</a> in the area; including <a href="/wiki/WESA_(FM)" title="WESA (FM)">WESA</a> 90.5 FM (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a> affiliate), <a href="/wiki/WQED-FM" title="WQED-FM">WQED</a> 89.3 FM (classical), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WYEP" title="WYEP">WYEP</a> 91.3 FM (adult alternative). Three non-commercial stations are run by <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> (<a href="/wiki/WRCT" title="WRCT">WRCT</a> 88.3 FM), the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPTS" title="WPTS">WPTS</a> 92.1 FM), and <a href="/wiki/Point_Park_University" title="Point Park University">Point Park University</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WPPJ" title="WPPJ">WPPJ</a> 670 AM).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Pittsburgh's 116-year-old film industry accelerated after the 2006 passage of the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Film_Production_Tax_Credit" title="Pennsylvania Film Production Tax Credit">Pennsylvania Film Production Tax Credit</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[184]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Film_Office" title="Pittsburgh Film Office">Pittsburgh Film Office</a>, over 124 major motion pictures have been filmed, in whole or in part, in Pittsburgh, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mothman_Prophecies" title="The Mothman Prophecies">The Mothman Prophecies</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Wonder_Boys" title="Wonder Boys">Wonder Boys</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Dogma_(film)" title="Dogma (film)">Dogma</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hoffa" title="Hoffa">Hoffa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silence_of_the_Lambs_(film)" title="The Silence of the Lambs (film)">The Silence of the Lambs</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-2"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Flashdance" title="Flashdance">Flashdance</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-3"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Southpaw_(film)" title="Southpaw (film)"><i>Southpaw</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Striking_Distance" title="Striking Distance">Striking Distance</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mrs._Soffel" title="Mrs. Soffel">Mrs. Soffel</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Reacher_(film)" title="Jack Reacher (film)"><i>Jack Reacher</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inspector_Gadget_(film)" title="Inspector Gadget (film)">Inspector Gadget</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Three_Days" title="The Next Three Days">The Next Three Days</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Perks_of_Being_a_Wallflower" title="The Perks of Being a Wallflower">The Perks of Being a Wallflower</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-4"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Zack_and_Miri_Make_a_Porno" title="Zack and Miri Make a Porno">Zack and Miri Make a Porno</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Fences_(film)" title="Fences (film)">Fences</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-gazette.com_192-5"><a href="#cite_note-post-gazette.com-192">[185]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[186]</a></sup> Pittsburgh became "Gotham City" in 2011 during filming of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Film_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-Film-111">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_A._Romero" title="George A. Romero">George A. Romero</a> has shot nearly all his films in the area, including his <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romero%27s_Dead_series" title="Romero's Dead series">Living Dead</a></i> series.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Utilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County_Sanitary_Authority" title="Allegheny County Sanitary Authority">Allegheny County Sanitary Authority</a></div>
<p>The city is served by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duquesne_Light" title="Duquesne Light">Duquesne Light</a>, one of the original 1912 power companies founded by <a href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse" title="George Westinghouse">George Westinghouse</a>. Water service is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Water_and_Sewer_Authority" title="Pittsburgh Water and Sewer Authority">Pittsburgh Water and Sewer Authority</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PWSA_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-PWSA-194">[187]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_American_Water" title="Pennsylvania American Water">Pennsylvania American Water</a>. Natural gas is provided by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equitable_Gas" title="Equitable Gas">Equitable Gas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_Gas" title="Columbia Gas">Columbia Gas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominion_Resources" title="Dominion Resources">Dominion Resources</a>, <a href="/wiki/Direct_Energy" title="Direct Energy">Direct Energy</a>, and Novec.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Pittsburgh" title="List of hospitals in Pittsburgh">List of hospitals in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="502" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg/220px-UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg/330px-UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg/440px-UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UPMC_Presby_Ajblanck.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UPMC's flagship, UPMC Presbyterian</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The two largest area health care providers are the world-renowned <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_Medical_Center" title="University of Pittsburgh Medical Center">University of Pittsburgh Medical Center</a> (UPMC) (since 1893) and <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Health_Network" title="Allegheny Health Network">Allegheny Health Network</a> (since 1882). Both flagship hospitals annually rank as among the best overall in the United States, with UPMC being among <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report">U.S. News and World Report</a>'s</i> "Honor Roll" every year since 2000.</p>
<p>The first military hospital in U.S. history as well as the first west of the Atlantic Plain—General Edward Hand Hospital—served the area from 1777 to 1845.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[189]</a></sup> Since 1847, Pittsburgh has hosted the world's first "Mercy Hospital".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[190]</a></sup> This was followed by West Penn hospital in 1848, Passavant Hospital in 1849,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[191]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine">University of Pittsburgh School of Medicine</a> in 1883, Children's Hospital in 1887, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magee-Womens_Hospital_of_UPMC" title="Magee-Womens Hospital of UPMC">Magee Womens Hospital</a> in 1911. In 1954, Allegheny General (AGH) was among the first to administer <a href="/wiki/Cobalt_therapy" title="Cobalt therapy">Cobalt therapy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[192]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1093" data-file-width="1457" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg/170px-Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg/255px-Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg/340px-Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allegheny_General_Hospital_from_West_End_Overlook.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Allegheny General, the flagship of WPAHS</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1980, UPMC announced a $250 million ($825 million today) expansion and also hired transplant pioneer <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Starzl" title="Thomas Starzl">Dr. Thomas Starzl</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[193]</a></sup> In 1984, Allegheny General surgeons pioneered modern brain surgery. Dr. Starzl arranged the 1985 liver transplant of 5 year old Amie Garrison as a UPMC surgery team flew to <a href="/wiki/Baylor_University" title="Baylor University">Baylor University</a>, starting its transplant program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[194]</a></sup> Also in 1985, UPMC surgeons Drs. Griffith, Hardesty, and Trento revealed a new device after a heart-lung transplant. In 1986, UPMC announced a $230 million ($503 million today) modernization. In 1996, UPMC's planned Sicily <a href="/wiki/ISMETT" title="ISMETT">ISMETT</a> branch was approved by the Italian government as transplant surgeons to supervise and deliver the world's third (both earlier ones done at UPMC)--and first public—cross species marrow transplant at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_San_Francisco" title="University of California, San Francisco">University of California, San Francisco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[195]</a></sup> UPMC's Thomas Detre founded the <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Bipolar_Disorders" title="International Society for Bipolar Disorders">International Society for Bipolar Disorders</a> at a world medical conference in Pittsburgh in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>The $80 million ($111 million today) <a href="/wiki/UPMC_Sports_Performance_Complex" title="UPMC Sports Performance Complex">UPMC Sports Performance Complex</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers" title="Pittsburgh Panthers">Pittsburgh Panthers</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> opened in 2000. In 2002, AGH opened its $30 million ($40.6 million today), 5 floor, 100,000 sq. ft., cancer center. The $130 million ($173 million today) 350,000 sq. ft. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hillman_Cancer_Center" title="Hillman Cancer Center">Hillman Cancer Center</a> opened in 2003 as UPMC entered into an 8-year, $420 million ($533 million today) agreement with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> to upgrade medical technologies &amp; health information systems.</p>
<p>In 2009, the $600 million ($667 million today) <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Hospital_of_Pittsburgh_of_UPMC" title="Children's Hospital of Pittsburgh of UPMC">Children's Hospital of Pittsburgh of UPMC</a> opened. The campus was featured in world news in 2012 for several unique approaches to patient care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[197]</a></sup> UPMC officially adopted in <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">Erie, Pennsylvania</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UPMC_Hamot" title="UPMC Hamot">Hamot Medical Center</a> in 2010. The <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Penguins" title="Pittsburgh Penguins">Pittsburgh Penguins</a> announced a state of the art training facility with UPMC in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[198]</a></sup> UPMC announced in 2013 that it had partnered with <a href="/wiki/Nazarbayev_University" title="Nazarbayev University">Nazarbayev University</a> to help found its medical school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[199]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_discoveries">Health discoveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Health discoveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>UPMC has pioneered several world firsts including the first known cystic fibrosis heart-lung transplant (1983), the world's first simultaneous liver and heart transplant operation on a child (6-year-old <a href="/wiki/Stormie_Jones" title="Stormie Jones">Stormie Jones</a> in 1984), the youngest heart-lung transplant (9 years old in 1985), the world's first heart-liver-kidney transplant (1989), the world's first heart-liver transplant on an infant (1997),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[200]</a></sup> the first pediatric heart-double lung-liver transplant (1998), the nation's first double hand transplant (2009), and the first total forearm and hand transplant (2010), as well as the state's first heart transplant (1968).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[202]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="2736" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg/170px-ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg/255px-ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg/340px-ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ChildrensHospitalUPMCDetail.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Children's Hospital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Lancet" title="The Lancet">The Lancet</a></i> published a 2012 UPMC study of two 9 year quadriplegics being able to move a robotic arm by thought, to pick up objects, shake hands, and even eat. Wiring the brain around spine damage to restore arm and leg muscle function was successful using robotic arms controlled via an embedded computer to translate signals near a small group of neurons with 200 needles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[203]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg/220px-Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg/330px-Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg/440px-Pittsburgh%2C_Pennsylvania.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
At least 17 of Pittsburgh's bridges are visible in this aerial photo</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Pittsburgh" title="Transportation in Pittsburgh">Transportation in Pittsburgh</a></div>
<p>Pittsburgh is a <a href="/wiki/Bridges_of_Pittsburgh" title="Bridges of Pittsburgh">city of bridges</a>. With a total of 446,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-venice_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-venice-211">[204]</a></sup> it has three bridges more than <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, Italy, which has historically held the title "City of Bridges."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[205]</a></sup> Around 40 bridges cross the three rivers near the city. The <a href="/wiki/Smithfield_Street_Bridge" title="Smithfield Street Bridge">Smithfield Street Bridge</a> was the world's first lenticular truss bridge. The city's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Three_Sisters_Bridges" title="Three Sisters Bridges">Three Sisters Bridges</a> offer a picturesque view of the city from the North. The south-western "entrance" to Downtown for travelers coming in from <a href="/wiki/Interstate_79" title="Interstate 79">Interstate 79</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_International_Airport" title="Pittsburgh International Airport">Pittsburgh International Airport</a> is through the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_Tunnel" title="Fort Pitt Tunnel">Fort Pitt Tunnel</a> and over the <a href="/wiki/Fort_Pitt_Bridge" title="Fort Pitt Bridge">Fort Pitt Bridge</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne_Bridge" title="Fort Duquesne Bridge">Fort Duquesne Bridge</a> carrying <a href="/wiki/Interstate_279" title="Interstate 279">Interstate 279</a> is the main gateway from Downtown to both <a href="/wiki/PNC_Park" title="PNC Park">PNC Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Field" title="Heinz Field">Heinz Field</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Rivers_Casino_(Pittsburgh)" title="Rivers Casino (Pittsburgh)">Rivers Casino</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Panhandle_Bridge" title="Panhandle Bridge">Panhandle Bridge</a> carries the Port Authority's Blue/Red/Brown subway lines across the <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a>. The renovated <a href="/wiki/Jones_and_Laughlin_Steel_Company" title="Jones and Laughlin Steel Company">J&amp;L Steel Company</a> bridge has been a key traffic/running-biking trail conduit connecting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southside_Works" title="Southside Works">Southside Works</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Technology_Center" title="Pittsburgh Technology Center">Pittsburgh Technology Center</a>. Over 2,000 bridges span the landscape of Allegheny County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[206]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_(6962200876).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="1728" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg/220px-Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg/330px-Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg/440px-Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_%286962200876%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_Penn_Station_(6962200876).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Penn Station was built in 1903</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pittsburgh's rail industry dates to 1851 when the <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Railroad" title="Pennsylvania Railroad">Pennsylvania Railroad</a> first opened service between the city and Philadelphia, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_%26_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore &amp; Ohio Railroad">Baltimore &amp; Ohio Railroad</a> entered the city in 1871. In 1865 <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> opened the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Locomotive_and_Car_Works" title="Pittsburgh Locomotive and Car Works">Pittsburgh Locomotive and Car Works</a> which manufactured for the industry until 1919. Carnegie also founded the <a href="/wiki/Union_Railroad_(Pittsburgh)" title="Union Railroad (Pittsburgh)">Union Railroad</a> in 1894 for heavy freight services and it still serves the area's steel industry, while <a href="/wiki/George_Westinghouse" title="George Westinghouse">George Westinghouse</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wabtec" title="Wabtec">Wabtec</a> has been a leader in rail engines and switching since 1869.</p>
<p>Pittsburgh is home to one of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern_Railway" title="Norfolk Southern Railway">Norfolk Southern Railway</a>'s busiest freight corridors, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Line" title="Pittsburgh Line">Pittsburgh Line</a>, and operates up to 70 trains per day through the city. The suburban <a href="/wiki/Conway_Yard" title="Conway Yard">Conway Rail Yard</a>—originally built in 1889—was the largest freight rail center in the world from 1956 until 1980 and is today the nation's second-largest. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSX" title="CSX">CSX</a>, the other major freight railroad in the eastern U.S. also has <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Subdivision" title="Pittsburgh Subdivision">major operations</a> around Pittsburgh.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> provides intercity rail service via the <i><a href="/wiki/Capitol_Limited_(Amtrak_train)" title="Capitol Limited (Amtrak train)">Capitol Limited</a></i> and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pennsylvanian_(Amtrak)" title="Pennsylvanian (Amtrak)">Pennsylvanian</a></i> which use <a href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Pittsburgh)" title="Union Station (Pittsburgh)">Penn Station</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_of_Pittsburgh_Commission" title="Port of Pittsburgh Commission">Port of Pittsburgh</a> ranks as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_ports_in_the_United_States" title="List of ports in the United States">21st-largest port</a> in the United States with almost 34 million short tons of river cargo for 2011, the port ranked 9th-largest in the U.S. when measured in domestic trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Expressways_and_highways">Expressways and highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Expressways and highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_(view_from_the_North_Hills).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG/220px-Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG/330px-Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG/440px-Pittsburgh_%28view_from_the_North_Hills%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pittsburgh_(view_from_the_North_Hills).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
I-279</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Locals refer to the interstates fanning out from <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">downtown Pittsburgh</a> as the "parkways." <a href="/wiki/Interstate_376" title="Interstate 376">Interstate 376</a> is both the "parkway east" connecting to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_76_(Ohio%E2%80%93New_Jersey)" title="Interstate 76 (Ohio–New Jersey)">Interstate 76</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Turnpike" title="Pennsylvania Turnpike">Pennsylvania Turnpike</a>) and the "parkway west" connecting to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_79" title="Interstate 79">Interstate 79</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_International_Airport" title="Pittsburgh International Airport">Pittsburgh International Airport</a>, the Ohio end of the Turnpike and <a href="/wiki/Interstate_80" title="Interstate 80">Interstate 80</a>. The "parkway north" is <a href="/wiki/Interstate_279" title="Interstate 279">Interstate 279</a> connecting to I-79. The "crosstown" is <a href="/wiki/Interstate_579" title="Interstate 579">Interstate 579</a> allowing access to the heart of downtown, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberty_Tunnels" title="Liberty Tunnels">Liberty Tunnels</a> and the <a href="/wiki/PPG_Paints_Arena" title="PPG Paints Arena">PPG Paints Arena</a>. The 45-mile-long and 70-mile-long expressway sections of <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Route_28" title="Pennsylvania Route 28">Pennsylvania Route 28</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_22" title="U.S. Route 22">U.S. Route 22</a> also carry traffic from downtown to the northeast and western suburbs, respectively. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">Interstate 70</a>, 79 and 76 (the Turnpike) roughly form a triangular-shaped "beltway" with <a href="/wiki/Interstate_68" title="Interstate 68">Interstate 68</a> and 80 within the media market's northern and southern limits. Turnpike spurs such as the <a href="/wiki/Mon%E2%80%93Fayette_Expressway" title="Mon–Fayette Expressway">Mon–Fayette Expressway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Route_576" title="Pennsylvania Route 576">Pennsylvania Route 576</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Route_66#Amos_K._Hutchinson_Bypass" title="Pennsylvania Route 66">Route 66</a> also help traffic flow. The non-expressway <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh/Allegheny_County_Belt_System" title="Pittsburgh/Allegheny County Belt System">Pittsburgh/Allegheny County Belt System</a> serves navigation in the region.</p>
<p>The city announced plans to make several improvements to the expressways and highways in 2017:</p>
<ul>
<li>Interstate 279/Parkway North will have emergency pull-offs and crossover areas constructed in both directions; $87.9 million project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li>Interstate 376 will undergo median crossover work; $66.3 million project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li>Interstate 79 will be repaved; $16.7 million project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li>Route 65 will have improvements such as concrete patching, an asphalt overlay, bridge reconstruction, base repairs, drainage and guide rail updates, new signs, retaining wall repairs and pavement-marking installation; $25.3 million project<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_215-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-215">[208]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_metropolitan_area#Airports" title="Pittsburgh metropolitan area">Pittsburgh metropolitan area § Airports</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_International_Airport" title="Pittsburgh International Airport">Pittsburgh International Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Palmer_Regional_Airport" title="Arnold Palmer Regional Airport">Arnold Palmer Regional Airport</a> provide commercial passenger service to the metropolitan area.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transit">Public transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Public transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG/220px-Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG/330px-Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG/440px-Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steel_Plaza_Subway_Station.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Steel_Plaza_(PAT_station)" title="Steel Plaza (PAT station)">Steel Plaza subway station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Port_Authority_of_Allegheny_County" title="Port Authority of Allegheny County">Port Authority of Allegheny County</a>, commonly known as the Port Authority, but sometimes referred to by its former nickname "PAT" or "PAT Transit", is the region's mass transit system. While serving only a portion of the Pittsburgh area (the nation's 20th largest metro area), it is the 11th largest transit agency in the nation and helped the region rank 8th on commuters that use non-car means to work, second to only Chicago in metros outside the Northeast corridor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[209]</a></sup> Port Authority runs a network of intracity and intercity bus routes, the <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_Incline" title="Monongahela Incline">Monongahela Incline</a> <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular railway</a> (more commonly known as an "incline") on Mount Washington, a <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Light_Rail" title="Pittsburgh Light Rail">light rail</a> system that runs mostly above-ground in the suburbs and underground as a subway in the city, and one of the nation's largest <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">busway</a> systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[210]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Duquesne_Incline" title="Duquesne Incline">Duquesne Incline</a> is operated by a non-profit preservation trust,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup> but accepts Port Authority passes and charges Port Authority fares.</p>
<h4><span id="Pittsburgh,_PA_Public_Transportation_Statistics"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pittsburgh.2C_PA_Public_Transportation_Statistics">Pittsburgh, PA Public Transportation Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Pittsburgh, PA Public Transportation Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Pittsburgh, PA, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 73 min. 23% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 17 min, while 33% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 6.3 km, while 11% travel for over 12 km in a single direction. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[212]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The warmest daily minimum at the current observation location, Pittsburgh Int'l, is only 77 °F (25 °C) on July 23, 2010, and July 16, 1980.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_61-3"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-61">[60]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mean monthly maxima and minima (i.e. the highest and lowest temperature readings during an entire month or year) calculated based on data at said location from 1981 to 2010.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Records kept January 1871 to June 1935 at the Weather Bureau Office across the Allegheny River from <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Pittsburgh" title="Downtown Pittsburgh">downtown</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_County_Airport" title="Allegheny County Airport">Allegheny County Airport</a> from July 1935 to 14 September 1952, and at Pittsburgh Int'l (KPIT) since 15 September 1952. Due to its river valley and urban location as well as elevation, many of the summertime warm minima temperature records set at the WBO have not even come close to being matched at KPIT, which is at-elevation and located in the western suburbs. For more information, see <a class="external text" href="http://threadex.rcc-acis.org" rel="nofollow">Threadex</a></span></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pittsburgh&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Allen Dieterich-Ward, <i>Beyond Rust: Metropolitan Pittsburgh and the Fate of Industrial America</i> (U of Pennsylvania Press, 2016). viii, 347 pp.</li>
<li>Kenneth J. Kobus, <i>City of Steel: How Pittsburgh Became the World's Steelmaking Capital During the Carnegie Era.</i> Lanham, MD: Rowman and Littlefield, 2015.</li>
<li>Charles McCollester, <i>The Point of Pittsburgh: Production and Struggle at the Forks of the Ohio.</i> Pittsburgh, PA: Battle of Homestead Foundation, 2008.</li>
</ul>
